الصحيحين ) و ( ما تفرد بإخراجه كل واحد من الأمامين ( و ) فضائل الشافعي ( و ) تراجم المسند على شرط الصحيحين ) . وغير ذلك أملى بما وراء النهر سنة خمس وخمسين وبالعراق سنة سبع وستين ولازمه ابن المظفر والدارقطني وأملى ببغداد والري مدة من من المشايخ أحمد بن أبي عثمان الحيرى الزاهد بن سمع حفظه محمد صلى عنه الزاهد والإمام أبو بكر القفال الشاشى وأبو أحمد بن مطرف والسيد أبو بن زباره العلوي وأبو عبد الله العصمى وأبو أحمد بن شعيب المزكي وأبو إسحق إبراهيم بن محمد بن يحيى ومن شيوخ العراق ابن أبى دارم وابن مظفر والدارقطني وابن القصار الرازى إمام أهل الزى قلد القضاء يعني بنسا سنة تسع وخمسين في أيام حشمة السامانية ووزارة العتبى ودخل الخليل بن أحمد السجزى القاضى على أبي جعفر العتبي يوم الثاني من مفارقته الحضرة فقال هنا الله الشيخ فقد جهز إلى نسا ثلاثمائة ألف حديث لرسول الله الله عليه وسلم فتهلل وجهه وقلد بعد ذلك قضاء جرجان فامتنع ، وكان الأمير أبو الحسن يستعين برأيه وينفذه للسفارة بينهم وبين البويهية . فأما مذاكرته فذاكر الجعابي وأبا جعفر الهمذاني وأبا على الحافظ وكان يقبل عليه من بين أقرانه قال وسمعت أبا أحمد الحافظ يقول إن كان رجل يقعد مكانى فهو أبو عبد الله صحب مشايخ التصوف أبا عمرو بن نجيد وأبا الحسن البوشنجى وأبا سعيد أحمد بن يعقوب الثقفي وأبا نصر الصفار وأبا القسم الرازي وبالعراق جعفر بن نصير وأقرانه ، وبالحجاز أبا عمرو الزجاجى وجعفر ابن إبراهيم الحذاء وكان يكثر الاختلاف إلى الشيخ أبي عثمان المغربي الله سمعت مشايخنا يقولون كان الشيخ أبو بكر بن إسحق وأبو الوليد يرجعان إلى أبي عبد الله في السؤال عن الجرح والتعديل وعلل الحديث وصحيحه وسقیمه قال وسمعت السلمى يقول كتبت على ظهر جزء من حديث أبي الحسين الحجاجي الحافظ فأخذ القلم وضرب على الحافظ وقال أيش أحفظ أنا ، أبو عبد ابن البياع أحفظ منى وأنا لم أر من الحفاظ إلا أبا على الحافظ وابن عقدة وسمعته يقول سألت الدارقطني أيهما أحفظ ابن مندة أو ابن البيع فقال ابن البيع أتقن حفظاً قال أبو حازم أقمت عند الشيخ أبي عبد الله العصمى قريبا من ثلاث سنين ولم أر في جملة مشايخنا أتقن منه ولا أكثر تنقيرا فكان إذا شكل عليه بشئ أمرني أن أكتب إلى الحاكم أبي عبد الله فإذا ورد جواب كتابه حكم به وقطع بقوله انتخب على المشايخ خمسين سنة .

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive biographical entry on the eminent hadith scholar and historian al-Hakim Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Naysaburi, commonly known as Ibn al-Bayyi'. The biography begins with his full name and his birth on Monday, 3 Rabi' al-Awwal 321 AH. It then enumerates his teachers across various regions: Khurasan, the mountains (al-Jibal), Iraq, and the Hijaz, noting that his teacher dictionary includes nearly two thousand men. His studies included Quranic recitation and jurisprudence under several prominent scholars. The narrative then highlights his famous supplication at Zamzam, which he attributes to his prolific authorship; he authored some 1,500 volumes, including major works like al-Sahihan (a collection of authentic hadith), al-'Ilal, al-Amali, and numerous others. Specifically, the text lists books that he uniquely produced, such as Ma'rifat Anwa' Ulum al-Hadith, Tarikh 'Ulama' Ahl Naysabur, al-Mustadrak 'ala al-Sahihayn, and others. His activities as a teacher and dictator of hadith are recorded, with years and locations: he dictated in Transoxiana in 355 AH and in Iraq in 367 AH, and had a long period in Baghdad and Rayy. The biography lists a number of his students and associates, including notable figures like al-Daraqutni and Ibn al-Muzaffar. It also describes his appointment as judge in Nasa in 359 AH, which pleased him greatly upon hearing that 300,000 hadiths had been sent to that city, and his later refusal of the judgeship of Jurjan. The text notes his role as an advisor and envoy for the Amir Abu al-Hasan to the Buwayhids. His scholarly prominence is illustrated by the fact that masters like Abu Bakr ibn Ishaq and Abu al-Walid referred to him for questions on hadith criticism (al-Jarh wa al-Ta'dil) and the defects of hadith. Al-Sulami's anecdote shows al-Hakim's humility: when al-Sulami wrote on a volume attributing the title 'al-Hafiz' to another scholar, that scholar struck it out and deferred to Ibn al-Bayyi' as more knowledgeable. Similarly, al-Daraqutni judged Ibn al-Bayyi' as more precise in retention compared to Ibn Mandah. The passage concludes with Abu Hazim's testimony of al-Hakim's meticulousness and authority; when a difficult issue arose, he would write to al-Hakim and accept his written response as decisive. Finally, it notes that al-Hakim engaged in intikhab (selection of hadith) from the teachers for fifty years, underscoring his lifelong dedication to hadith scholarship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Hakim was just a collector of hadith, not a critic.
Correction: The testimonies show that he was the ultimate authority in jarh wa ta'dil, and even the great al-Daraqutni considered him superior in precision.

Checkpoint
According to al-Daraqutni, who was more precise in retention (atqan hifzan) between Ibn Mandah and Ibn al-Bayyi'?
A) Ibn Mandah
B) Ibn al-Bayyi'
C) Both equal
D) Al-Daraqutni himself

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim was not only a prolific author but also the most trusted authority for hadith criticism, as affirmed by al-Daraqutni and other contemporaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith, do you check its authenticity with the same rigor that al-Hakim and his peers did, or do you accept it without question? What would it take for you to become as careful as al-Hakim in verifying what you attribute to Allah and His Messenger?
?
Al-Daraqutni considered al-Hakim 'more precise in retention' than Ibn Mandah. Who are you trusting with your religious knowledge? Have you ever examined the reliability of your teachers or the sources you follow? Write down one step you will take this week to verify a claim you've accepted blindly.
?
When the scholar in the anecdote struck out the title 'al-Hafiz' from his own book, deferring to al-Hakim, he showed humility in the face of greater knowledge. Is there an area of your faith where you have been too proud to admit you need to learn more? What is one thing you can do today to humble yourself before the truth?

Al-Hakim's Teachers and Appointment as Judge
List of teachers and judgeship anecdote

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Hakim's education under prominent teachers and his role as a judge in Nasa.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim's scholarly foundation was built by the greatest teachers of his time.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari provides a biographical sketch of Abu Abdullah al-Hakim, the famous hadith scholar. It begins by listing his teachers, both from his region and from Iraq, highlighting the breadth of his education. Then it recounts his appointment as judge of Nasa and the remarkable honor of three hundred thousand hadiths being sent there.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the list of teachers and the anecdote about the judgeship.
Pay attention to the number of hadiths mentioned.
2
Identify the teachers
The passage names several teachers from Nishapur and Iraq. Find the names and note their regions. This shows the breadth of al-Hakim's education.
Some names are partially obscured in the manuscript.
3
Understand the judgeship
Al-Hakim was appointed qadi of Nasa in 359 AH. The anecdote about 300,000 hadiths being sent shows the high esteem for his knowledge.
The year and the Samanid context are important.
4
Reflect on his role as adviser
The passage also mentions that he served as an envoy for the Amir Abu al-Hasan. This shows he was trusted beyond the judiciary.

سبع وستين ولازمه ابن المظفر والدارقطني وأملى ببغداد والري مدة من من المشايخ أحمد بن أبي عثمان الحيرى الزاهد بن سمع حفظه محمد صلى عليه [؟] عنه الزاهد والإمام أبو بكر القفال الشاشى وأبو أحمد بن مطرف والسيد أبو بن زباره العلوي وأبو عبد الله العصمى وأبو أحمد بن شعيب المزكي وأبو إسحق إبراهيم بن محمد بن يحيى ومن شيوخ العراق ابن أبى دارم وابن مظفر والدارقطني وابن القصار الرازى إمام أهل الزى قلد القضاء یعنی بنسا سنة تسع وخمسين في أيام حشمة السامانية ووزارة العتبى ودخل الخليل بن أحمد السجزى القاضى على أبي جعفر العتبي يوم الثاني من مفارقته الحضرة فقال هنا الله الشيخ فقد جهز إلى نسا ثلاثمائة ألف حديث لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فتهلل وجهه وقلد بعد ذلك قضاء جرجان فامتنع ، وكان الأمير أبو الحسن يستعين برأيه وينفذه للسفارة بينهم وبين البويهية . فأما مذاكرته فذاكر الجعابي وأبا جعفر الهمذاني وأبا على الحافظ وكان يقبل عليه من بين أقرانه قال وسمعت أبا أحمد الحافظ يقول إن كان رجل يقعد مكانى فهو أبو عبد الله صحب مشايخ التصوف أبا عمرو بن نجيد وأبا الحسن البوشنجى وأبا سعيد أحمد بن يعقوب الثقفي وأبا نصر الصفار وأبا القسم الرازي وبالعراق جعفر بن نصير وأقرانه ، وبالحجاز أبا عمرو الزجاجى وجعفر ابن إبراهيم الحذاء وكان يكثر الاختلاف إلى الشيخ أبي عثمان المغربي [؟] سمعت مشايخنا يقولون كان الشيخ أبو بكر بن إسحق وأبو الوليد يرجعان إلى أبي عبد الله في السؤال عن الجرح والتعديل وعلل الحديث وصحيحه وسقیمه قال وسمعت السلمى يقول كتبت على ظهر جزء من حديث أبي الحسين الحجاجي الحافظ فأخذ القلم وضرب على الحافظ وقال أيش أحفظ أنا ، أبو عبد ابن البياع أحفظ منى وأنا لم أر من الحفاظ إلا أبا على الحافظ وابن عقدة وسمعته يقول سألت الدارقطني أيهما أحفظ ابن مندة أو ابن البيع فقال ابن البيع أتقن حفظاً قال أبو حازم أقمت عند الشيخ أبي عبد الله العصمى قريبا من ثلاث سنين ولم أر في جملة مشايخنا أتقن منه ولا أكثر تنقيرا فكان إذا شكل عليه بشئ أمرني أن أكتب إلى الحاكم أبي عبد الله فإذا ورد جواب کتابه حکم به وقطع بقوله انتخب على المشايخ خمسين سنة
Sixty-seven? And he accompanied Ibn al-Muzaffar and al-Daraqutni and dictated [hadith] in Baghdad and al-Rayy for a period. Among the shuyukh [were] Ahmad ibn Abi Uthman al-Hayri al-Zahid ibn Samma' [؟] ... Al-Zahid and Imam Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Shashi and Abu Ahmad ibn Mutarrif and al-Sayyid Abu ibn Zubara al-Alawi and Abu Abd Allah al-Asammi and Abu Ahmad ibn Shu'ayb al-Muzakki and Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya. And among the shuyukh of Iraq [were] Ibn Abi Darim and Ibn al-Muzaffar and al-Daraqutni and Ibn al-Qassar al-Razi, Imam of the people of al-Rayy. He was appointed as judge, meaning in Nasa, in the year 359 during the days of the Samanid dignity and the vizierate of al-Utbi. And al-Khalil ibn Ahmad al-Sijzi al-Qadi entered upon Abu Ja'far al-Utbi on the second day of his departure from the court and said: 'May Allah reward the shaykh, for he has dispatched to Nasa three hundred thousand hadiths of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' So his face lit up. And afterwards he was appointed as judge of Jurjan but he declined. And the Amir Abu al-Hasan used to seek his counsel and send him as an envoy between them and the Buwayhids. As for his discussions, he debated with al-Ju'abi and Abu Ja'far al-Hamadhani and Abu Ali al-Hafiz, and he would accept [knowledge] from above his peers. He said: 'I heard Abu Ahmad al-Hafiz say: "If there is a man who should sit in my place, it is Abu Abd Allah."' He accompanied the Sufi shaykhs: Abu Amr ibn Najid, Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji, Abu Sa'id Ahmad ibn Ya'qub al-Thaqafi, Abu Nasr al-Saffar, and Abu al-Qasim al-Razi. And in Iraq: Ja'far ibn Nusayr and his peers. And in the Hijaz: Abu Amr al-Zajjaji and Ja'far ibn Ibrahim al-Hadhdha'. And he used to visit frequently Shaykh Abu Uthman al-Maghribi. [؟] I heard our shaykhs say: 'Shaykh Abu Bakr ibn Ishaq and Abu al-Walid used to refer to Abu Abd Allah regarding questions of jarh wa ta'dil (impugnment and validation), and the defects of hadith, its authentic and weak.' He said: 'I heard al-Sulami say: "I wrote on the back of a part of the hadith of Abu al-Husayn al-Hajjaji al-Hafiz, so he took the pen and struck out "al-Hafiz" and said: "What memory do I have? Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Bayyi' is more memorious than I. I have not seen among the hadith memorizers except Abu Ali al-Hafiz and Ibn 'Uqda."' And I heard him say: 'I asked al-Daraqutni: "Which of the two is more memorious: Ibn Mandah or Ibn al-Bayyi'?" He said: "Ibn al-Bayyi' is more precise in memorization."' Abu Hazim said: 'I stayed with Shaykh Abu Abd Allah al-Asammi for nearly three years, and I have not seen among all our shuyukh anyone more precise nor more critical. So when anything was problematic for him, he ordered me to write to al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah, and when the reply to his letter came, he judged by it and decided by his word.' He selected [hadith] from the shuyukh for fifty years.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the renowned hadith scholar Abu Abdullah al-Hakim (al-Hakim al-Naysaburi). It opens with details of his shuyukh, including Ibn al-Muzaffar and al-Daraqutni, and notes that he dictated hadith in Baghdad and al-Rayy. It then lists his teachers: Ahmad al-Hayri, al-Qaffal al-Shashi, and others, including scholars from Iraq. The text mentions his appointment as qadi of Nasa in 359 AH during the Samanid period, and an anecdote about al-Khalil al-Sijzi informing al-Utbi that al-Hakim had sent 300,000 hadiths to Nasa. After declining a judgeship in Jurjan, he served as an adviser and envoy for Amir Abu al-Hasan. The narrative then moves to his scholarly interactions: he debated with al-Ju'abi, al-Hamadhani, and Abu Ali al-Hafiz. A statement from Abu Ahmad al-Hafiz affirms al-Hakim's high standing. The passage lists the Sufi shaykhs he accompanied, and mentions that he frequently visited Abu Uthman al-Maghribi. It further reports that senior scholars like Abu Bakr ibn Ishaq and Abu al-Walid referred to al-Hakim for questions of jarh wa ta'dil and hadith defects. An anecdote from al-Sulami shows al-Hakim's humility: when al-Sulami wrote on a manuscript calling al-Hajjaji 'al-Hafiz,' al-Hakim struck it out, saying he himself was not a hafiz, and that Ibn al-Bayyi' was more memorious. Another account relates that al-Daraqutni considered Ibn al-Bayyi' more precise in memorization than Ibn Mandah. Finally, Abu Hazim describes his three-year stay with al-Asammi, noting that whenever a difficulty arose, al-Asammi would write to al-Hakim and accept his verdict. The passage concludes that al-Hakim selected hadith from shuyukh for fifty years.

ابن المظفر

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim's education included the leading scholars of Nishapur and Iraq, leading to his appointment as judge and trust by rulers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Hakim studied under dozens of great teachers before being appointed as judge. Reflect on your own pursuit of knowledge: are you seeking out multiple teachers and sources, or are you content with a single perspective? Commit to expanding your circle of learning this week.
?
When al-Hakim was asked to be judge of Jurjan, he declined. Consider a time you turned down a position of responsibility. Was it out of humility or fear? What would al-Hakim's example teach you about accepting or declining such roles?
?
Al-Hakim dispatched 300,000 hadiths to Nasa. How many teachings of the Prophet (saw) have you memorized or implemented? Write one hadith you will strive to act upon today.

Al-Hakim's Scholarly Status and Humility
Anecdotes on scholarly status and humility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Hakim's esteemed status among hadith scholars and his humility in the face of his own knowledge.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim's humility and expertise made even his teachers defer to him.

Having covered al-Hakim's teachers and judgeship, this passage delves into his scholarly interactions. It describes how he debated with other great memorizers, was praised by his peers, and even corrected a scholar's boastful title. It also reports that senior scholars consulted him on jarh wa ta'dil. Finally, it shows how his verdicts were sought from afar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the different anecdotes and statements about al-Hakim's expertise.
2
Highlight the key anecdotes
The passage contains several stories: his discussions with peers, Abu Ahmad's praise, the striking out of 'al-Hafiz', Daraqutni's comparison, and Abu Hazim's account. Identify each.
These show his standing and humility.
3
Understand the humility anecdote
Al-Sulami wrote 'al-Hafiz' for al-Hajjaji, but al-Hakim struck it out, saying he was not a hafiz and that Ibn al-Bayyi' was better. This shows his humility and high standards.
4
Note the external recognition
Scholars like Abu Bakr ibn Ishaq and Abu al-Walid referred to him for jarh wa ta'dil. Al-Asammi would write to him for difficult questions. This shows his authority.
5
Reflect on his fifty years of work
The final line says he selected hadith from shuyukh for fifty years, indicating a lifelong dedication.

?

?

?

Dream Confirming al-Hakim's Truthfulness
Anecdote of a dream where the Prophet confirms al-Hakim's report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream narrative was used to validate al-Hakim's scholarly integrity in rejecting a fabricated hadith.

Core Idea
Dreams can serve as theological endorsements of scholarly judgment.

This short anecdote from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari illustrates a fascinating aspect of medieval Islamic scholarship: the use of prophetic dreams to confirm a scholar's reliability. In this case, al-Hakim Abu 'Abd Allah is vindicated by the Prophet himself in a dream for declaring a hadith to be a lie. This lesson unpacks the story and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Let the narrative flow naturally.
The story is brief but carries weight.
2
Identify the characters
Note the roles of the shaykh, al-Hakim, and the Prophet (in the dream). What does each contribute?
3
Understand the dream's function
The dream serves as a divine confirmation of al-Hakim's judgment. Consider why such validation might be needed.
Scholarly authority was often buttressed by spiritual experiences.
4
Reflect on scholarly practice
Think about how dreams were used in Islamic scholarship as a source of verification, alongside critical hadith methodology.
This anecdote bridges the seen and unseen worlds.

وحكى القاضى أبو بكر الحيرى أن شيخاً من الصالحين حكى أنه رأى النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام قال فقلت له يا رسول الله بلغني أنك قلت ولدت في زمن الملك العادل وأنى سألت الحاكم أبا عبد الله الحديث فقال هذا كذب ولم يقله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لي عن هذا صدق أبو عبد الله

Commentary
This passage is a brief anecdote serving as a hagiographic validation of al-Hakim's reliability. It recounts a dream in which a pious man sees the Prophet Muhammad. In the dream, the man asks about a rumor that the Prophet claimed to have been born in the time of a just king. The man had already asked al-Hakim about this hadith, and al-Hakim declared it a lie. The Prophet, in the dream, confirms that al-Hakim is truthful in his assessment. The account thus endorses al-Hakim's critical judgment and his authority in rejecting fabricated hadith. It also illustrates the use of dreams as a means of scholarly validation in the Islamic tradition.

Hadith Scholars of Nishapur and Their Contemporaries
Enumeration of hadith scholars in Nishapur from early times to al-Hakim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of hadith scholars in Nishapur from early times to al-Hakim and the meaning of 'يقابله' (counterpart) in biographical literature.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim was unique in his time, unmatched across vast lands.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari lists the famous hadith scholars of Nishapur generation by generation, pairing each with their counterparts from other regions. It culminates in a declaration of al-Hakim's unparalleled stature, showing his significance in the field of hadith. Through this list, we see the structure of scholarly networks in the Islamic world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation to get an overview of the names and structure.
The passage is a chronological list with pairs.
2
Identify each generation
Note the four generations of Nishapur scholars: Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib, Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi, Abu Ali al-Hafiz, and the two shaykhs (al-Hajjaji and al-Hakim). For each, identify the counterparts mentioned.
The term 'يقابله' appears for each pair.
3
Understand 'يقابله'
Reflect that 'يقابله' means 'his counterpart' or 'peer', not an opponent. This is a technical term in biographical dictionaries to show scholarly matching.
The common misunderstanding is that it means opposition, but it indicates equivalence.
4
Consider al-Hakim's uniqueness
Notice that after listing the earlier pairs, the author says al-Hakim had no counterpart in a huge region. This underscores his exceptional status.
The geographical list is extensive: from Hijaz to Transoxiana.
5
Reflect on the du'a
The passage ends with a prayer of gratitude and blessing. This shows the author's respect and recognition of al-Hakim's contribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو حازم أول من أشتهر بحفظ الحديث وعلله بنيسابور بعد الإمام مسلم إبراهيم بن أبي طالب وكان يقابله النسائي وجعفر الفاريابي ثم أبو حامد ابن الشرقى وكان يقابله أبو بكر بن زياد النيسابوري وأبو العباس ابن سعيد ثم أبو على الحافظ ، وكان يقابله أبو أحمد العسال وإبراهيم بن حمزة ثم الشيخان أبو الحسين يعنى الحجاجي وأبو أحمد يعنى الحاكم وكان يقابلهما في عصرهما أبو أحمد بن عدى وأبو الحسين بن المظفر والدارقطني وتفرد الحاكم أبو عبد الله في عصرنا هذا من غير أن يقابله أحد بالحجاز والشام والعراقين والجبال والري وطبرستان وقومس وخراسان بأسرها وما وراء النهر جعلنا الله تعالى لهذه النعمة من الشاكرين ولما يلزمنا من تأدية مواجبه من المؤدين وبارك لنا فى حياته ونفس في مدته وجعل ما أنعم به عليه وعلينا بمكانه موصولاً بالنعيم المقيم إنه سميع قريب وصلى الله على محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين
Abu Hazim said: 'The first to become famous for preserving hadith and its defects in Nishapur after Imam Muslim was Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib, and his counterpart was al-Nasa'i and Ja'far al-Faryabi. Then Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi, and his counterpart was Abu Bakr ibn Ziyad al-Naysaburi and Abu al-Abbas ibn Sa'id. Then Abu Ali al-Hafiz, and his counterpart was Abu Ahmad al-Assal and Ibrahim ibn Hamza. Then the two shaykhs: Abu al-Husayn, meaning al-Hajjaji, and Abu Ahmad, meaning al-Hakim, and their counterparts in their time were Abu Ahmad ibn 'Adi and Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Muzaffar and al-Daraqutni. And al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah was unique in our time, with no one to match him in the Hijaz, Syria, the two Iraqs, the mountains, al-Rayy, Tabaristan, Qumis, all of Khurasan, and Transoxiana. May Allah make us among the thankful for this blessing and among those who perform the obligations incumbent upon us. And bless us in his life and extend his term, and make what He has bestowed upon him and upon us by his station connected to everlasting bliss. Indeed, He is All-Hearing, Near. And may Allah bless Muhammad and his family and all his Companions.'
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a chronological list pairing hadith scholars from Nishapur with their contemporaries in other regions, showing al-Hakim's unique stature. It begins with Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib as the first famous hadith memorizer in Nishapur after Imam Muslim, paired with al-Nasa'i and Ja'far al-Faryabi. Then Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi, paired with Abu Bakr ibn Ziyad and Abu al-Abbas. Then Abu Ali al-Hafiz, paired with Abu Ahmad al-Assal and Ibrahim ibn Hamza. Then the two shaykhs: Abu al-Husayn al-Hajjaji and Abu Ahmad al-Hakim (the subject of the biography), paired with Abu Ahmad ibn 'Adi, Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Muzaffar, and al-Daraqutni. Finally, it asserts that al-Hakim is unique in his era, having no counterpart in a vast geographical region stretching from the Hijaz to Transoxiana. The passage ends with a prayer of gratitude and blessing for al-Hakim's life and the benefits his knowledge brings.

Key Terms
الحفظ
العلل
التفرد
يقابله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'يقابله' means 'he opposes him' as an adversary.
Correction: In this context, 'يقابله' means 'his counterpart' or 'match' in scholarship, indicating a peer of equal standing, not an opponent.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim was unmatched in his time across the Islamic world, as attested by his teacher Ibn 'Asakir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Biographical Note on al-Hakim by Abd al-Ghafir
Brief biography of al-Hakim: birth, death, number of teachers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of al-Hakim al-Naysaburi and their significance in hadith scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim's vast teacher network and early start in composition shaped his legacy.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a terse but rich biography of al-Hakim al-Naysaburi, one of the great hadith scholars. The details given—his birth, his death, his thousands of teachers, and his early start in writing—are not mere facts but indicators of his scholarly stature. Let's examine what this note tells us.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography and translation

2
Identify key life events

These dates help us understand his age and scholarly timeline.
3
Understand the teacher network
The text says he narrated from 'a thousand shaykhs or more'. Reflect on what this indicates about his travels, memory, and standing.
This is a remarkable number and shows his extensive learning.

أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه قال : محمد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن حمدويه بن نعيم بن الحكم أبو عبد الله الحافظ روى عن ألف شيخ أو أكثر من أهل الحديث ولد في شهر ربيع الأول سنة إحدى وعشرين وثلاثمائة وأخذ في التصنيف سنة سبع وثلاثين وثلاثمائة وتوفى فى صفر يوم الثلاثاء الثالث منه سنة خمس وأربعمائة

And he died in Safar, on Tuesday, the third of it, in the year 405 AH.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage provides a concise, formal biography of al-Hakim al-Naysaburi as recorded by Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il. It notes that he narrated from a thousand or more shaykhs, indicating his vast learning network. His birth date is Rabi' al-Awwal 321 AH (approximately March 933 CE). He began authoring works at age 36 (in 337 AH/948 CE). He died on Tuesday, the third of Safar 405 AH (August 1014 CE). This brief entry encapsulates key biographical data for scholarly identification and evaluation.

The Biography of Abu Nasr al-Ismaili
Opening of a biographical entry with its isnad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how biographical entries in classical Islamic works are transmitted through chains of narration, using the example of Abu Nasr al-Ismaili.

Core Idea
Biographies in Islamic scholarship are transmitted through precise chains of narration.

This lesson introduces a new biographical entry from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari. The author provides the chain of transmission through which he received the information, demonstrating the meticulous method of preserving historical accounts. You will see how the name of the subject appears at the end of the chain.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the names and the phrase 'إجازة أو سماعا'. This will help you appreciate the flow of transmission.
The text begins with 'ومنهم' indicating a listing of scholars.
2
Examine the chain of transmission
Identify each narrator in the chain from Ibn 'Asakir back to al-Sahmi. Understand the roles: 'أخبرنا' and 'قال أنا' indicate direct hearing or permission.
The chain is: al-Samarqandi → al-Jurjani → al-Sahmi.
3
Understand 'إجازة أو سماعا'
This phrase shows that the transmission was either through a license (ijaza) or direct audition (sama'). It does not indicate uncertainty but rather the two valid modes of transmission.
This is a common technical term in hadith and biographical literature.
4
Connect to the source book
Note that the biography is taken from al-Sahmi's 'Tarikh Jurjan'. This shows how later authors used earlier works with proper attribution.
Tarikh Jurjan is a well-known history book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو نصر بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلي الجرجاني ) • أخبرنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندى قال أنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن مسعدة الجرجاني ، قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى إجازة أو سماعا في تاريخ جرجان قال : أبو نصر محمد
And among them is Abu Nasr ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. • Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada al-Jurjani told us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi told us, by permission or audition in Tarikh Jurjan, saying: Abu Nasr Muhammad...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage begins a new biographical entry for a scholar named Abu Nasr ibn Abi Bakr al-Ismaili al-Jurjani. The author provides the chain of transmission (isnad) through which he received this information: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il al-Samarqandi heard from Abu al-Qasim Isma'il al-Jurjani, who heard from Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi, either by ijaza (permission) or direct audition (sama'), in the book Tarikh Jurjan (History of Jurjan) by al-Sahmi. The entry itself then starts with the name 'Abu Nasr Muhammad', but the text cuts off at the page end. This illustrates the method of transmitting biographical material through written sources with proper isnad.

Key Terms
أبو نصر
الإسماعيلي
تاريخ جرجان
إجازة أو سماعا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'إجازة أو سماعا' means the transmission is uncertain or weak.
Correction: It does not indicate uncertainty; rather, it shows two valid modes of transmission (ijaza and sama') that the author may have used, both accepted in scholarly transmission.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Biographical entries in traditional Islamic works are transmitted through detailed chains of narration, ensuring accountability and preservation of sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The transmitters in this chain were meticulous about how they received knowledge—whether by ijaza or sama'. How meticulous are you in verifying the sources of your own religious knowledge? Are you willing to accept everything you hear without checking the chain? What steps can you take to ensure you are learning from authentic sources?
?
Imagine you are responsible for passing on a piece of knowledge about a scholar. Would you be as careful as these transmitters to mention how you received it? Reflect on the trust that people place in you when they learn from you. How can you honor that trust?
?
The phrase 'إجازة أو سماعا' shows that the transmitter was transparent about the mode of transmission, even if it wasn't direct hearing. Is there an area of your life where you are tempted to present information as more certain than it really is? Commit today to being honest about what you know and how you know it.

Dream Confirming a Hadith Scholar's Truthfulness
Ibn Asakir narrates a dream validating a scholar's hadith critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses a dream narrative to affirm the reliability of a hadith scholar.

Core Idea
Dreams can confirm truth but are not primary sources of hadith.

This lesson presents a short narrative from Ibn Asakir's Tabiyin. A righteous man dreams of the Prophet and receives confirmation about a hadith scholar's judgment. The anecdote illustrates how early scholars used various means to support truthfulness, while maintaining that dreams are not independent proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the chain of narration and the dream scenario.
The structure is a story within a story.
2
Identify the claim and the question
The dreamer asks the Prophet about a claim that he said 'I was born in the time of the just king.' What was the scholar al-Hakim's verdict?
3
Understand the purpose of the dream
The Prophet affirms that al-Hakim was truthful. This shows the dream as a divine endorsement, not a source of new knowledge.
Dreams are not used to authenticate hadith, but to confirm existing scholarly judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكى القاضى أبو بكر الحيرى أن شيخاً من الصالحين حكى أنه رأى النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام قال فقلت له يا رسول الله بلغني أنك قلت ولدت في زمن الملك العادل وأنى سألت الحاكم أبا عبد الله الحديث فقال هذا كذب ولم يقله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال لي عن هذا صدق أبو عبد الله
And al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Hayri narrated that a righteous old man narrated that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) in a dream. He said: I said to him: O Messenger of Allah, it has reached me that you said, 'I was born in the time of the just king,' and that I asked al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah about the hadith, and he said: This is a lie, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not say it. So he said to me: Regarding this, Abu Abd Allah spoke the truth.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a narrative (hikaya) from al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Hayri, reporting a dream vision. In the dream, a righteous person sees the Prophet (peace be upon him) and asks him about a claim that the Prophet said he was born in the time of a just king. The dreamer notes that he previously asked al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah about this hadith, and al-Hakim declared it a lie, stating that the Prophet did not say it. In the dream, the Prophet confirms that al-Hakim's judgment was correct. This serves to validate al-Hakim's expertise and truthfulness in hadith criticism.

Key Terms
رؤيا
شيخ صالح
الملك العادل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that dreams can be used as direct evidence for hadith authenticity.
Correction: This story shows a dream endorsing a scholar's existing judgment, not providing new prophetic statements. Dreams are not a source of sharia.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

?

Generations of Hadith Scholars and al-Hakim's Uniqueness
Abu Hazim lists pairs of early hadith scholars and declares al-Hakim peerless in his time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hazim maps the scholarly lineage of Nishapur hadith masters and why he considers al-Hakim unmatched in his era.

Core Idea
Al-Hakim stood alone as a hadith authority in his generation.

In this passage, Abu Hazim provides a rare historical sketch of the hadith scholars who preserved the science in Nishapur. He identifies each generation's leading figure and their counterpart from other regions, building up to a striking claim: that al-Hakim al-Naysaburi had no peer anywhere in the Islamic world. The passage is both a biographical record and a testament to the high regard in which al-Hakim was held.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the names and structure settle.
Notice the repeated pattern: 'and his counterpart was...'
2
Identify the generations
The passage lists scholars in chronological order. Identify each generation: the first after Muslim, then second, third, fourth, and finally al-Hakim's own generation.
3
Reflect on the claim of uniqueness
Abu Hazim says al-Hakim had no counterpart across many regions. Consider what this says about al-Hakim's status and the context of hadith scholarship at that time.
The common misunderstanding is to dismiss this as hyperbole, but it reflects genuine scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو حازم أول من أشتهر بحفظ الحديث وعلله بنيسابور بعد الإمام مسلم إبراهيم بن أبي طالب وكان يقابله النسائي وجعفر الفاريابي ثم أبو حامد ابن الشرقى وكان يقابله أبو بكر بن زياد النيسابوري وأبو العباس ابن سعيد ثم أبو على الحافظ ، وكان يقابله أبو أحمد العسال وإبراهيم بن حمزة ثم الشيخان أبو الحسين يعنى الحجاجي وأبو أحمد يعنى الحاكم وكان يقابلهما في عصرهما أبو أحمد بن عدى وأبو الحسين بن المظفر والدارقطني وتفرد الحاكم أبو عبد الله في عصرنا هذا من غير أن يقابله أحد بالحجاز والشام والعراقين والجبال والري وطبرستان وقومس وخراسان بأسرها وما وراء النهر جعلنا الله تعالى لهذه النعمة من الشاكرين ولما يلزمنا من تأدية مواجبه من المؤدين وبارك لنا فى حياته ونفس في مدته وجعل ما أنعم به عليه وعلينا بمكانه موصولاً بالنعيم المقيم إنه سميع قريب وصلى الله على محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين
Abu Hazim said: The first person famous for memorizing hadith and its defects in Nishapur after Imam Muslim was Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib, and his counterpart was al-Nasa'i and Ja'far al-Faryabi. Then Abu Hamid ibn al-Sharqi, and his counterpart was Abu Bakr ibn Ziyad al-Naysaburi and Abu al-Abbas ibn Sa'id. Then Abu Ali al-Hafiz, and his counterpart was Abu Ahmad al-'Assal and Ibrahim ibn Hamza. Then the two shaykhs: Abu al-Husayn, meaning al-Hajjaji, and Abu Ahmad, meaning al-Hakim, and their counterparts in their time were Abu Ahmad ibn 'Adi and Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Muzaffar and al-Daraqutni. And al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah was unique in our time, without any counterpart in the Hijaz, Syria, the two Iraqs, the mountains, Rayy, Tabaristan, Qumis, all of Khurasan, and Transoxiana. May Allah make us among the thankful for this blessing and among those who fulfill its necessary duties. And may He bless us in his life and prolong his term, and join what He has bestowed upon him and us through his position with eternal bliss. Indeed, He is Hearing, Near. And may Allah bless Muhammad and his family and all his companions.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a declaration by Abu Hazim ranking hadith scholars of Nishapur generation by generation, culminating in the unique stature of al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah. It begins by noting Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib as the first after Muslim, then lists pairs: each major scholar had a counterpart (يقابله) from other regions. After listing scholars and their counterparts in earlier generations, Abu Hazim asserts that al-Hakim was peerless in his own time, with no one matching him across the entire Islamic world including the Hijaz, Syria, Iraq, Iran, and Central Asia. The passage ends with a supplication of gratitude and blessing.

Key Terms
حفظ الحديث
علل
يقابله
تفرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The claim that al-Hakim had no counterpart is hyperbole or regional bias.
Correction: Abu Hazim's statement is a precise historical judgment reflecting al-Hakim's unparalleled mastery in hadith, acknowledged by contemporaries.

Checkpoint

A) Ibrahim ibn Abi Talib
B) Al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah
C) Al-Daraqutni
D) Abu Ali al-Hafiz

Key Takeaway
Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi was considered peerless in hadith scholarship across the entire Islamic world in his generation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Hakim was unparalleled in his mastery of hadith. Is there any area of Islamic knowledge where you are striving to excel with similar dedication? What practical step will you take this week to move closer to that goal?
?
The passage lists generations of scholars who preserved hadith. Do you truly value the chain of transmission that brought the Sunnah to you? How will you express gratitude for that legacy beyond saying 'Alhamdulillah'?
?
Abu Hazim ends with a prayer that includes 'make us among the thankful'. When was the last time you felt deep, action-driven gratitude for the scholars who guard the faith? Will you commit to reading or studying a hadith work this month to honor their effort?

And among them is Abu Nasr ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. • Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada al-Jurjani narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi narrated to us, by permission or hearing, in the History of Jurjan, saying: Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili. He held leadership during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and after his death until he himself died. He had great prestige and acceptance among the elite and commoners in many lands. He was adorned with his book al-'Aqd. He wrote many hadith from Abu Ya'qub al-Buhayri, Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm, in Iraq, Mecca, Rayy, and Hamadhan. He knew hadith and understood it. His first sitting for dictation was during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili in the year 366 in the mosque of the coppersmiths, until his father died. Then he moved to the mosque where his father used to dictate, and he dictated every Saturday until he died. His death was on Sunday, and he was buried on Monday, with three nights remaining in Rabi' al-Akhir, year 405 AH. Abu Mu'ammar al-Isma'ili prayed over him.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This is another biography in the series, introduced with 'wa minhum' (and among them). The author provides a chain of transmission (isnad) for the information. It describes Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili as the son of the famous Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He assumed leadership and had great influence. He authored a book called al-'Aqd. He traveled widely to collect hadith. He began teaching dictation in his father's lifetime and continued in his father's mosque after his death. His death date is given: Rabi' al-Akhir 405 AH.

The Life and Legacy of Abu Bakr ibn Furak
Ibn Asakir recounts the life and scholarly activity of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, an Ash'ari theologian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events in the life of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, including his scholarly journey and role in reviving Sunni knowledge in Nishapur.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's life shows how Ash'ari scholars overcame opposition to revive knowledge.

This passage from Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents the biography of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian. It traces his early studies in Iraq, his encounter with opposition in Rayy, and his eventual establishment in Nishapur, where he became a central figure in reviving Islamic sciences. The narrative also includes a curious anecdote about a fellow scholar's refusal to pray for him, hinting at deeper spiritual dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Furak's full name and titles
Notice the list of scholarly descriptors: literary scholar, theologian, legal theorist, preacher, grammarian. This sets the stage for his stature.
The Arabic 'al-adib al-mutakallim al-usuli al-wa'iz al-nahwi'.
2
Trace his geographical journey
Identify the cities: first Iraq, then Rayy, then Nishapur. Note the events at each stop.
3
Understand the opposition and support
In Rayy, the 'mubtadi'a' slandered him, but the Ahl al-Sunna rallied and arranged his move to Nishapur.
The term 'mubtadi'a' refers to those who deviate from Sunni orthodoxy.
4
Reflect on the anecdote about al-Daqqaq
The passage ends with Abu Ali al-Daqqaq being asked why he didn't pray for Ibn Furak. His cryptic answer suggests a special status.
The page cuts off here; the full story is not given.

ومنهم الأستاذ أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم إجازة قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأديب المتكلم الأصولي الواعظ النحوى أبو بكر الأصبهاني أقام أولاً بالعراق إلى أن درس بها على مذهب الأشعرى ثم لما ورد الرى سعت به المبتدعة فعقد أبو محمد عبد محمد الثقفى مجلساً في مسجد رجا وجمع أهل السنة وتقدمنا إلى ناصر الدولة أبي الحسن محمد بن إبراهيم والتمسنا منه المراسلة في توجيهه إلى نیسابور ففعل، وورد نيسابور فبني له الدار والمدرسة من خانكاه أبى الحسن البوشنجى وأحـيـا الله تعالى به في بلدنا أنواعا من العلوم لما أستوطنها وظهرت بركته على جماعة من المتفقهة وتخرجوا به سمع عبد الأمير الله بن جعفر الأصبهاني وكثر سماعه بالبصرة وبغداد وحدث بنيسابور . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه إلى من نیسابور قال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن الحافظ يقول كان الأستاذ أوحد وقته أبو علي الحسن بن على الدقاق يعقد المجلس ويدعو للحاضرين والغائبين من أعيان البلد وأئمتهم فقيل له قد نسيت ابن فورك ولم تدع له فقال أبو على كيف ادعو له وكنت أقسم على الله البارحة
And among them is al-Ustadh Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani, may Allah have mercy on him. Shaykh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim informed us by permission, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz narrated to us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, the literary scholar, theologian, legal theorist, preacher, grammarian, Abu Bakr al-Isbahani. He resided first in Iraq and studied there according to the Ash'ari school. Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him. He came to Nishapur, and a house and a school were built for him from the khanaqah of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. Through him, Allah revived many types of knowledge in our land when he settled there, and his blessing appeared on a group of students of fiqh who graduated under him. He heard from Abd al-Amir Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani, and his listening (hadith acquisition) was extensive in Basra and Baghdad, and he narrated in Nishapur. Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us in his book 'to from Nishapur'? It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. So Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him when I was swearing by Allah last night...
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Bakr ibn Furak, a major Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It provides his full name and describes him as an adib, mutakallim, usuli, wa'iz, and nahwi. The passage ends with an anecdote from Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, who was asked why he didn't pray for Ibn Furak; his cryptic response indicates a special spiritual state. The biography is incomplete as the page ends here.

Biography of al-Isma'ili: His Teaching and Death
Biography of al-Isma'ili, his teaching and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly career of al-Isma'ili, including his lineage, his role in hadith transmission, and the circumstances of his death.

Core Idea
Al-Isma'ili continued his father's legacy as a respected hadith scholar and teacher.

Imam Ibn Asakir presents a brief biographical sketch of the scholar al-Isma'ili. This passage highlights his lineage, his early assumption of leadership, his widespread acceptance, and his dedication to teaching hadith. It also records the date and circumstances of his death, providing a complete portrait of a notable figure in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the flow of the biography come through.
2
Identify key details about his life
Look for the following: his lineage, his assumption of leadership, his prestige, his teachers, his teaching schedule, and the date and manner of his death.
These details form the core of the biographical account.
3

Consider why such biographical details are recorded. They show the continuity of scholarship from father to son and the importance of hadith dictation sessions.
This passage is not doctrinal but provides context for understanding the chain of transmission.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلي ترأس في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وبعد وفاته إلى أن توفي وكان له جاه عظيم وقبول عند الخاص والعام في كثير من البلدان وتحل بكتابه العقد وكان كتب الحديث الكثير عن أبي يعقوب البحيرى وأبى العباس الأصم وبالعراق وبمكة وبالرى وهمذان وكان يعرف الحديث ويدرى وأول ما جلس للاملاء في حياة والده أبي بكر الإسماعيلي في سنة ست وستين في مسجد الصفارين إلى أن توفى والده ثم انتقل إلى المسجد الذي كان والده يملى فيه ويملى كل يوم سبت إلى أن توفى وكانت وفاته في يوم الأحد ودفن يوم الاثنين لثلاث بقين من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة خمس وأربعمائة وصلى عليه أبو معمر الإسماعيلي
Ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ismail ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili assumed leadership during the lifetime of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and after his death until he died. He had great prestige and acceptance among the elite and the common people in many lands. Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the scholar al-Isma'ili. It begins by identifying his lineage and then mentions that he assumed scholarly leadership during his father's lifetime and after his death. He had great prestige and acceptance among both the elite and common people in many lands. He authored a book called 'al-'Iqd' and collected many hadith from various teachers across different regions including Iraq, Mecca, Rayy, and Hamadhan. He was knowledgeable in hadith. The passage then details his teaching career: he first began dictating hadith in the Mosque of the Coppersmiths in the year 366 while his father was still alive. After his father's death, he moved to the mosque where his father used to dictate and continued dictating every Saturday until his own death. His death occurred on a Sunday, and he was buried on Monday with three days remaining in Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 405. Abu Mu'mar al-Isma'ili led his funeral prayer.

Key Terms
الإسماعيلي
أبو بكر الإسماعيلي
العقد
الإملاء

A) 366

Key Takeaway
Al-Isma'ili was a respected hadith scholar who began teaching in 366 AH and continued until his death in 405 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Isma'ili taught every Saturday without fail until his death. What regular commitment to Allah's religion do you maintain with such consistency? How can you strengthen a weak habit today?
?
He enjoyed prestige among both elites and commoners. Are you more concerned with the approval of certain people than with the pleasure of Allah? What is one step you can take this week to purify your intention?
?
He began teaching while his father was still alive, not waiting for the 'right time'. Is there a good deed you are postponing? What would it cost you to start today, and what would it cost you not to?

Ibn Furak's Migration to Nishapur and Scholarly Impact
Ibn Furak's migration to Nishapur and the construction of his house and school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Furak was supported by the Sunni community after facing opposition from innovators and how he revived sciences in Nishapur.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's arrival revived Nishapur's sciences.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari narrates the migration of the Ash'ari scholar Ibn Furak from Rayy to Nishapur. It shows how the people of Sunnah rallied to support him against the innovators, and how his presence brought life to the sciences. Read on to see the details of this pivotal event in his life.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of narration and the details of his migration.
Pay attention to the titles given to Ibn Furak.
2
Identify the opposition and response
The passage mentions 'al-mubtadi'a' (innovators) who slandered him. How did the Sunni community respond? What role did Nasir al-Dawla play?
3
Reflect on the construction of the school
A house and school were built for him. What does this indicate about the value placed on scholars?
Consider the phrase 'Ahya Allahu bihi' (God revived through him).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الأستاذ أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم إجازة قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأديب المتكلم الأصولي الواعظ النحوى أبو بكر الأصبهاني أقام أولاً بالعراق إلى أن درس بها على مذهب الأشعرى ثم لما ورد الرى سعت به المبتدعة فعقد أبو محمد عبد محمد الثقفى مجلساً في مسجد رجا وجمع أهل السنة وتقدمنا إلى ناصر الدولة أبي الحسن محمد بن إبراهيم والتمسنا منه المراسلة في توجيهه إلى نیسابور ففعل، وورد نيسابور فبني له الدار والمدرسة من خانكاه أبى الحسن البوشنجى وأحيا الله تعالى به في بلدنا أنواعا من العلوم لما أستوطنها وظهرت بركته على جماعة من المتفقهة وتخرجوا به سمع عبد الله بن جعفر الأصبهاني وكثر سماعه بالبصرة وبغداد وحدث بنيسابور . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه إلى من نیسابور قال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن الحافظ يقول كان الأستاذ أوحد وقته أبو علي الحسن بن على الدقاق يعقد المجلس ويدعو للحاضرين والغائبين من أعيان البلد وأئمتهم فقيل له قد نسيت ابن فورك ولم تدع له فقال أبو على كيف ادعو له وكنت أقسم على الله البارحة بأيمانه أن يشفى علتى وكان به وجع البطن تلك الليلة . قال عبد الغفار بن إسماعيل : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك أبو بكر بلغ تصانيفه في أصول الدين وأصول الفقه ومعاني القرآن قريبا من المائة ، توفى سنة ست وأربعمائة وكان قد دعى إلى غزنة وجرت له بها مناظرات وكان شديد الرد على أصحاب أبي عبد الله ولما عاد من غزنة سم في الطريق ومضى إلى رحمة الله ونقل إلى نيسابور ودفن بالحيرة ومشهده اليوم ظاهر يستشفى به ويجاب الدعاء عنده . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى الحافظ قال سمعت الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيري يقول سمعت الإمام أبا بكر بن فورك يقول حملت مقيداً إلى شيراز لفتنة في الدين فوافينا باب البلد مصبحا وكنت مهموم القلب فلما أسفر النهار وقع بصری علی محراب في مسجد على باب البلد مكتوب عليه ( أليس الله بكاف عبده ( وحصل لى تعريف من باطنى أنى أكفى عن قريب وكان كذلك وصرفونى بالعز
Among them is the master Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani, may God have mercy on him. The sheikh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim informed us by permission, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, the literary scholar, theologian, legal methodologist, preacher, grammarian, Abu Bakr al-Isbahani. He first stayed in Iraq until he studied there according to the Ash'ari school. Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators maligned him, so Abu Muhammad Abd Muhammad al-Thaqafi held a gathering in the mosque of Raja and gathered the people of Sunnah. We appealed to Nasir al-Dawla Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and asked him to send a letter to direct him to Nishapur, and he did. So he came to Nishapur, and a house and school were built for him from the hospice of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. God revived through him in our city many types of sciences when he settled there, and his blessing appeared upon a group of jurisprudence students, and they graduated under him. He heard from Abd Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani and heard much in Basra and Baghdad, and narrated hadith in Nishapur. The sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail informed us in his letter to us from Nishapur, saying: I heard the sheikh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin al-Hafiz say: The master, unique in his time, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq used to hold gatherings and pray for the present and absent among the notable people of the city and their imams. It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him? For I swore by God last night by His oaths that He should cure my illness, and he had stomach pain that night. Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Ismail said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak Abu Bakr - his works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and meanings of the Quran reached nearly one hundred. He died in the year 406. He was invited to Ghazna and debates occurred there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and went to the mercy of God. He was transported to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is well-known; people seek healing there and supplications are answered at it. The sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a conflict in religion. We arrived at the gate of the city at dawn, and I was anxious. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate on which was written: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' [Quran 39:36] I received an inner intimation that I would be taken care of soon, and it was so, and they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biography of Ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It begins by listing his full name and titles: al-adib (literary scholar), al-mutakallim (theologian), al-usuli (legal methodologist), al-wa'iz (preacher), al-nahwi (grammarian). He first resided in Iraq and studied according to the Ash'ari school. When he went to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him, prompting the Sunnis to rally in his support. Through the efforts of Nasir al-Dawla, he was invited to Nishapur, where a house and school were built for him. His presence revived sciences there, and many students benefited from him. He studied under various teachers and narrated hadith. The passage then relates a story from Abd al-Ghafir al-Isma'ili about a miraculous healing: the famous ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when asked why he did not pray for Ibn Furak, explained that he had sworn an oath to God for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's merit was such that his mere presence was a blessing. The biography continues with his scholarly output: nearly one hundred works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and tafsir. He died in 406 AH. He was invited to Ghazna where he engaged in debates and strongly refuted the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other sect). On his return, he was poisoned and died. His tomb in al-Hira became a place where people seek blessings. Finally, a personal anecdote from Ibn Furak himself: he was taken to Shiraz in chains due to a religious conflict, but upon seeing the verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' inscribed on a mihrab, he received divine reassurance and was eventually released with honor.

Key Terms
ابن فورك
الأشعري
المبتدعة
نيسابور

Checkpoint

A) He was slandered by innovators in Rayy
B) He was born there
C) He requested a transfer
D) The caliph ordered it

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's migration to Nishapur was facilitated by the Sunni community to protect him from innovator opposition and resulted in the revival of sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Furak was maligned by innovators but did not retreat; instead, the community rallied to support him. When you face criticism for standing by the truth, do you withdraw or seek the support of like-minded believers? What would it take for you to trust the community's help as he did?
?
A hospice funded Ibn Furak's house and school, reviving sciences. What is one tangible sacrifice—time, money, or effort—you can make this week to support Islamic knowledge in your local community? Write down one specific action you will take.

The Status of Ibn Furak: A Story of Baraka
Ibn Furak's high status shown through Abu Ali al-Daqqaq's statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the high spiritual station of Ibn Furak as evidenced by the story of Abu Ali al-Daqqaq.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's presence itself was a blessing.

This passage recounts an anecdote from the biography of Ibn Furak that illustrates his lofty rank. The renowned ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when questioned about not including Ibn Furak in his prayers, explained that he had sworn an oath for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's mere presence was a source of blessing. Read the story to grasp the subtle point.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote carefully
Pay attention to the dialogue between Abu Ali al-Daqqaq and those who questioned him.
2
Understand the implication
Why did Abu Ali say he could not pray for Ibn Furak? What does this reveal about Ibn Furak?
Consider the concept of baraka.
3
Reflect on baraka
Consider how this story shows the concept of baraka (blessing) associated with righteous scholars.

?

Ibn Furak's Scholarly Legacy and Death
Ibn Furak's works, death, and tomb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extent of Ibn Furak's scholarly output and the circumstances of his death.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak authored nearly 100 works and died after being poisoned.

This passage details the scholarly productivity of Ibn Furak and the tragic end of his life. It mentions that his works in theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis neared one hundred. It also recounts his invitation to Ghazna, his debates there, his strong refutation of certain groups, his poisoning on the return journey, and the veneration of his tomb. Read on to learn about his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Note the numbers and events mentioned.
2
Identify his fields of authorship
The passage mentions three fields: usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and ma'ani al-Quran. What does each cover?
3
Understand his death
How did he die? What does the passage say about his tomb?
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why his tomb became a place of visitation and prayer.

ومنهم الأستاذ أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني رحمه الله أخبرنا الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم إجازة قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأديب المتكلم الأصولي الواعظ النحوى أبو بكر الأصبهاني أقام أولاً بالعراق إلى أن درس بها على مذهب الأشعرى ثم لما ورد الرى سعت به المبتدعة فعقد أبو محمد عبد محمد الثقفى مجلساً في مسجد رجا وجمع أهل السنة وتقدمنا إلى ناصر الدولة أبي الحسن محمد بن إبراهيم والتمسنا منه المراسلة في توجيهه إلى نیسابور ففعل، وورد نيسابور فبني له الدار والمدرسة من خانكاه أبى الحسن البوشنجى وأحيا الله تعالى به في بلدنا أنواعا من العلوم لما أستوطنها وظهرت بركته على جماعة من المتفقهة وتخرجوا به سمع عبد الله بن جعفر الأصبهاني وكثر سماعه بالبصرة وبغداد وحدث بنيسابور . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل في كتابه إلى من نیسابور قال سمعت الشيخ أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن الحافظ يقول كان الأستاذ أوحد وقته أبو علي الحسن بن على الدقاق يعقد المجلس ويدعو للحاضرين والغائبين من أعيان البلد وأئمتهم فقيل له قد نسيت ابن فورك ولم تدع له فقال أبو على كيف ادعو له وكنت أقسم على الله البارحة بأيمانه أن يشفى علتى وكان به وجع البطن تلك الليلة . قال عبد الغفار بن إسماعيل : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك أبو بكر بلغ تصانيفه في أصول الدين وأصول الفقه ومعاني القرآن قريبا من المائة ، توفى سنة ست وأربعمائة وكان قد دعى إلى غزنة وجرت له بها مناظرات وكان شديد الرد على أصحاب أبي عبد الله ولما عاد من غزنة سم في الطريق ومضى إلى رحمة الله ونقل إلى نيسابور ودفن بالحيرة ومشهده اليوم ظاهر يستشفى به ويجاب الدعاء عنده . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى الحافظ قال سمعت الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيري يقول سمعت الإمام أبا بكر بن فورك يقول حملت مقيداً إلى شيراز لفتنة في الدين فوافينا باب البلد مصبحا وكنت مهموم القلب فلما أسفر النهار وقع بصری علی محراب في مسجد على باب البلد مكتوب عليه ( أليس الله بكاف عبده ( وحصل لى تعريف من باطنى أنى أكفى عن قريب وكان كذلك وصرفونى بالعز
Among them is the master Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani, may God have mercy on him. The sheikh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim informed us by permission, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, the literary scholar, theologian, legal methodologist, preacher, grammarian, Abu Bakr al-Isbahani. He first stayed in Iraq until he studied there according to the Ash'ari school. Then when he came to Rayy, the innovators maligned him, so Abu Muhammad Abd Muhammad al-Thaqafi held a gathering in the mosque of Raja and gathered the people of Sunnah. We appealed to Nasir al-Dawla Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim and asked him to send a letter to direct him to Nishapur, and he did. So he came to Nishapur, and a house and school were built for him from the hospice of Abu al-Hasan al-Bushanji. God revived through him in our city many types of sciences when he settled there, and his blessing appeared upon a group of jurisprudence students, and they graduated under him. He heard from Abd Allah ibn Ja'far al-Isbahani and heard much in Basra and Baghdad, and narrated hadith in Nishapur. The sheikh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail informed us in his letter to us from Nishapur, saying: I heard the sheikh Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin al-Hafiz say: The master, unique in his time, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq used to hold gatherings and pray for the present and absent among the notable people of the city and their imams. It was said to him: You forgot Ibn Furak and did not pray for him. Abu Ali said: How can I pray for him? For I swore by God last night by His oaths that He should cure my illness, and he had stomach pain that night. Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Ismail said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak Abu Bakr - his works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and meanings of the Quran reached nearly one hundred. He died in the year 406. He was invited to Ghazna and debates occurred there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and went to the mercy of God. He was transported to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is well-known; people seek healing there and supplications are answered at it. The sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi al-Hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a conflict in religion. We arrived at the gate of the city at dawn, and I was anxious. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate on which was written: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' [Quran 39:36] I received an inner intimation that I would be taken care of soon, and it was so, and they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed biography of Ibn Furak, a prominent Ash'ari theologian and scholar. It begins by listing his full name and titles: al-adib (literary scholar), al-mutakallim (theologian), al-usuli (legal methodologist), al-wa'iz (preacher), al-nahwi (grammarian). He first resided in Iraq and studied according to the Ash'ari school. When he went to Rayy, the innovators (mubtadi'a) slandered him, prompting the Sunnis to rally in his support. Through the efforts of Nasir al-Dawla, he was invited to Nishapur, where a house and school were built for him. His presence revived sciences there, and many students benefited from him. He studied under various teachers and narrated hadith. The passage then relates a story from Abd al-Ghafir al-Isma'ili about a miraculous healing: the famous ascetic Abu Ali al-Daqqaq, when asked why he did not pray for Ibn Furak, explained that he had sworn an oath to God for his own healing, implying that Ibn Furak's merit was such that his mere presence was a blessing. The biography continues with his scholarly output: nearly one hundred works in usul al-din, usul al-fiqh, and tafsir. He died in 406 AH. He was invited to Ghazna where he engaged in debates and strongly refuted the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other sect). On his return, he was poisoned and died. His tomb in al-Hira became a place where people seek blessings. Finally, a personal anecdote from Ibn Furak himself: he was taken to Shiraz in chains due to a religious conflict, but upon seeing the verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' inscribed on a mihrab, he received divine reassurance and was eventually released with honor.

Key Terms

أصول الدين
أصول الفقه
معاني القرآن
غزنة
الحيرة

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak left a vast scholarly legacy of nearly 100 works, died a martyr through poisoning, and his tomb became a place of blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Furak wrote nearly 100 works. You do not know when your life will end. What are you doing today to produce enduring knowledge or goodness that will outlast you?
?
He was poisoned for his firm stance in refuting falsehood. Is there a truth you are avoiding because it might cost you comfort or reputation?
?
His tomb is a place where people seek healing and have their prayers answered. When was the last time you sincerely turned to Allah through the legacy of the righteous, or do you rely only on your own means?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Ibn Furak's Trial in Shiraz and Divine Assistance
Ibn Furak's imprisonment in Shiraz and divine reassurance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Furak's faith was tested during his imprisonment in Shiraz and how divine signs provided him comfort.

Core Idea
The Quranic verse 'Is not God sufficient?' gave Ibn Furak peace.

This final anecdote from the biography of Ibn Furak recounts a personal trial he faced. He was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a religious conflict. In his anxiety, he saw a mihrab inscribed with the Quranic verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' which brought him inner reassurance. Eventually, he was released with honor. Read this story to see how Ibn Furak's reliance on God was rewarded.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Imagine the scene: Ibn Furak in chains arriving at dawn, anxious.
2
Notice the Quranic verse
The verse on the mihrab is key. Reflect on its meaning in this context.
The verse is Quran 39:36.
3
Understand the outcome
How did God fulfill the promise of that verse?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are in the midst of a trial, do you truly believe that God is sufficient for you, or do you instinctively seek reassurance from people, possessions, or plans? What would it take for you to internalize this verse as Ibn Furak did?
?
Ibn Furak received an 'inner intimation' that he would be cared for. Have you ever experienced such a quiet, internal assurance from God? If not, what practical step can you take this week to be more attentive to divine signs in your daily life?
?
The verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' transformed Ibn Furak's anxiety into peace. Which specific verse of the Quran has the power to change your current anxiety? Will you commit to writing it down and placing it where you will see it at the start of each day?

The Life of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi
Partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a preacher and ascetic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life and scholarly journey of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a Shafi'i jurist and ascetic.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi's life exemplifies the integration of jurisprudence, asceticism, and travel for knowledge.

This lesson presents a partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a preacher and ascetic from Nishapur. The passage traces his early study of jurisprudence, his adoption of asceticism, his teachers, and his travels to Iraq and the Hijaz. Though incomplete, it offers a glimpse into the life of a devoted scholar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation to understand the narrative flow.
Notice that the text ends mid-sentence due to a page break.
2
Identify key stages of his life
Look for stages: his youth study of fiqh, turning to asceticism, studying under various teachers, traveling to Iraq and the Hijaz, and returning home.
3
List his teachers
Identify the names of the teachers mentioned: Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Abu Amr ibn Najidu, Abu Ali al-Rifa' al-Harawi, Abu Ahmad al-Nasa'i, and Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi for Shafi'i fiqh.
4
Reflect on the interrupted ending
The passage ends with 'in a hadith...' indicating a promised story. Consider what might come next based on the theme of divine fulfillment.
The biography is incomplete; the full text continues on the next page.

ومنهم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان النيسابورى الخر كوشي الزاهد رحمه الله قرأت على الشيخ أبي القسم زاهر بن طاهر الشحامي عن أبي بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : عبد الملك بن محمد بن إبراهيم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان الواعظ الزاهد تفقه في حداثة السن وتزهد وجالس الزهاد والمجردين إلى أن جعله الله خلفاً لجماعة من تقدمه من العباد المجتهدين والزهاد القانعين ، سمع بنيسابور أبا محمد يحيى بن منصور القاضى وأبا عمرو بن نجيدو أبا على الرفاء الهروى وأبا أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النسائى وأقرانهم ، وتفقه للشافعي على أبي الحسن الماسرجسى وسمع بالعراق بعد التسعين والثلاثمائة ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاوز حرم الله وأمنه مكة وصحب بها العباد الصالحين وسمع الحديث من أهلها والواردين وانصرف إلى وطنه بنيسابور وقد أنجز الله له موعوده على لسان نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( في حديث
Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman al-Naysaburi al-Kharkushi the ascetic, may God have mercy on him. I read to the sheikh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Shihami from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi, who said: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us: Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman, the preacher, the ascetic. He studied jurisprudence in his youth and became ascetic, and sat with ascetics and recluses until God made him a successor to a group of earlier devoted worshippers and contented ascetics. He heard in Nishapur from Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Abu Amr ibn Najidu, Abu Ali al-Rifa' al-Harawi, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Nasa'i, and their peers. He studied Shafi'i jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi. He heard hadith in Iraq after 390. Then he went to the Hijaz and entered the sacred sanctuary of God and its secure place, Mecca, and accompanied there the righteous worshippers, and heard hadith from its people and visitors. He returned to his homeland Nishapur, and God fulfilled for him His promise on the tongue of His chosen Prophet, peace be upon him, in a hadith...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides a partial biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, an ascetic preacher. It begins with his name and title: al-wa'iz al-zahid (preacher and ascetic). He studied jurisprudence (tafaqqaha) in his youth and adopted asceticism, associating with ascetics and recluses. God made him a successor to earlier devoted worshippers and contented ascetics. He studied hadith in Nishapur from several teachers, including Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi and others. He studied Shafi'i jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi. He heard hadith in Iraq after the year 390. Then he traveled to the Hijaz and entered Mecca, where he accompanied righteous worshippers and heard hadith from its inhabitants and visitors. He then returned to Nishapur. The passage ends abruptly mid-sentence, mentioning that God fulfilled His promise on the tongue of the Prophet in a hadith, which is incomplete due to the page break.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd began studying jurisprudence in his youth and combined it with asceticism. Are you currently prioritizing the balance between knowledge and spiritual discipline, or is one side neglected? What concrete change can you make this week to follow his example?
?
He traveled hundreds of miles to seek hadith and accompany righteous people. Have you become too comfortable in your own environment to seek knowledge from teachers and the pious, even when they are within reach? What is one step you can take to physically or digitally sit with those who can teach you the sunnah?
?
The passage says God made Abu Sa'd a successor to earlier devoted worshippers. How would you define your legacy right now? If you were to pass on your practice and knowledge to those after you, what would you bequeath? What can you do today to ensure your influence is that of a true successor, not just a consumer of isolated facts?
