Ibn Furak: Scholar and the Miracle of Divine Sufficiency
Biography of Ibn Furak with anecdote of his release from prison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly legacy of Ibn Furak and the miraculous event that demonstrated Allah's sufficiency for His servant.

Core Idea
Allah's promise of sufficiency can manifest even in chains.

Ibn Furak was a towering Ash'ari scholar whose works spanned theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin presents both his scholarly contributions and a personal anecdote of his miraculous release from imprisonment. The story illustrates how divine assurance can turn distress into honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical overview
Read the first part of the passage, which lists Ibn Furak's scholarly works, his invitation to Ghazna, his death, and his burial place. Notice the high output of nearly a hundred works and the mention of his tomb as a site of healing.
This section establishes Ibn Furak's prominent status in Islamic scholarship.
2
Analyze the miraculous release narrative
Read the anecdote transmitted through al-Qushayri. Identify the Quranic verse Ibn Furak saw and the inner assurance he received. Observe the outcome: he was released with honor.
The verse 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' is key to the story.
3
Reflect on the core message
Consider how the anecdote demonstrates the principle of tawakkul (trust in God). Reflect on how divine sufficiency can manifest in difficult circumstances.
This connects the historical event to a universal spiritual lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال عبد الغفار بن إسماعيل : محمد بن الحسن بن فورك أبو بكر بلغ تصانيفه في أصول الدين وأصول الفقه ومعاني القرآن قريبا من المائة ، توفى سنة ست وأربعمائة وكان قد دعى إلى غزنة وجرت له بها مناظرات وكان شديد الرد على أصحاب أبي عبد الله ولما عاد من غزنة سم في الطريق ومضى إلى رحمة الله ونقل إلى نيسابور ودفن بالحيرة ومشهده اليوم ظاهر يستشفى به ويجاب الدعاء عنده .
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى الحافظ قال سمعت الأستاذ أبا القسم القشيري يقول سمعت الإمام أبا بكر بن فورك يقول حملت مقيداً إلى شيراز لفتنة في الدين فوافينا باب البلد مصبحا وكنت مهموم القلب فلما أسفر النهار وقع بصری علی محراب في مسجد على باب البلد مكتوب عليه ( أليس الله بكاف عبده ( وحصل لى تعريف من باطنى أنى أكفى عن قريب وكان كذلك وصرفونى بالعز .
Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Isma'il said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak, Abu Bakr, his works in usul al-din (foundations of religion), usul al-fiqh (foundations of jurisprudence), and ma'ani al-Qur'an (meanings of the Qur'an) reached nearly a hundred. He died in the year 406 AH. He had been invited to Ghazna and held debates there, and he was severe in refuting the followers of Abu Abd Allah. When he returned from Ghazna, he was poisoned on the road and passed to the mercy of God. He was transferred to Nishapur and buried in al-Hira. His tomb today is visible, where people seek healing and prayers are answered. 
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi the hafiz told us, saying: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard Imam Abu Bakr ibn Furak say: I was taken in chains to Shiraz due to a religious trial. We arrived at the gate of the city in the morning, and my heart was distressed. When the day brightened, my eyes fell upon a mihrab in a mosque at the city gate, on which was written: "Is not God sufficient for His servant?" (Qur'an 39:36). An inner realization came to me that I would be released soon, and so it happened; they released me with honor.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the renowned Ash'ari theologian Ibn Furak. It first provides his full name and his scholarly output in theology, jurisprudence, and Quranic exegesis. It notes his death in 406 AH. The text highlights his debates in Ghazna and his strong refutation of the followers of Abu Abd Allah (likely the Mu'tazila or other opponents). Upon his return from Ghazna, he was poisoned, died, and was buried in Nishapur. The passage emphasizes that his tomb is a place where people seek healing and where supplications are answered, indicating veneration. 
Then follows a first-person anecdote from Ibn Furak himself, transmitted through a chain: al-Bayhaqi from al-Qushayri. Ibn Furak recounts being arrested and taken in chains to Shiraz for a religious controversy. As he arrived at the city gate, he noticed a Quranic verse inscribed in a mosque: 'Is not God sufficient for His servant?' He felt an inner assurance that he would be freed soon, and indeed he was released with honor. This story serves to demonstrate divine intervention and the efficacy of trust in God.

أصول الفقه
معاني القرآن
غزنة
نيسابور
الحيرة
استشفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage justifies tomb worship or seeking healing directly from the deceased.
Correction: The text merely reports that people visit Ibn Furak's tomb for healing and prayer; it does not prescribe such acts as religious obligations or indicate that the dead grant requests.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's life and release demonstrate that divine sufficiency can transform moments of distress into honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial that seems overwhelming, do you genuinely believe that Allah is sufficient for you, or do you rely on your own strategies and resources? What one concrete step can you take today to deepen your trust in His promise of sufficiency?
?
Ibn Furak found solace in a familiar verse inscribed in a mosque. Is there a verse or reminder from Allah that you have repeatedly encountered but ignored? Write it down and commit to meditating on it daily this week, asking Allah to grant you inner assurance.
?
His release was with honor despite being brought in chains. Are you willing to endure temporary humiliation or difficulty for the sake of your faith, trusting that Allah can turn your distress into honor? What fear of loss or shame holds you back from full reliance on Him?

Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi: A Model of Asceticism and Service
Biography of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi including his life, charities, and hadith on divine love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and virtues of Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, focusing on his asceticism, charitable works, and the hadith about divine love that shaped his mission.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi turned divine love into a life of service.

This biography introduces a towering figure of Nishapur: Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi, a scholar and ascetic whose life mirrored the hadith that when God loves a servant, acceptance spreads throughout heaven and earth. As you read, notice how his personal transformation led to vast charitable projects and lasting scholarly works.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography fully
Read the Arabic and English passages once to get a sense of his life journey from youth to legacy.
Pay attention to the hadith of Suhayl – it’s central to understanding his motivation.
2
Map his life stages
Identify the main phases: early study and asceticism, travels to Iraq and Mecca, return to Nishapur, and his charitable and scholarly works.
3
Analyze the hadith and its impact
Study the hadith about God’s love and how al-Kharkushi interpreted it as a call to action. Notice the chain of transmission and the emphasis on acceptance on earth.
The hadith is quoted directly; reflect on why the author includes it.
4
List his charitable contributions
Identify the specific institutions he built: mosques, cisterns, bridges, a hospital, and his care for the poor and sick.
Note the detail about appointing caregivers for the sick.
5
Reflect on his legacy
Consider how the author praises him as unmatched in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance. What made him unique?
The passage ends with another chain of transmission confirming his identity.

ومنهم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان النيسابورى الخر كوشی الزاهد
رحمه الله
قرأت على الشيخ أبي القسم زاهر بن طاهر الشحامي عن أبي بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقى قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ قال : عبد الملك بن محمد بن إبراهيم أبو سعد بن أبي عثمان الواعظ الزاهد تفقه في حداثة السن وتزهد وجالس الزهاد والمجردين إلى أن جعله الله خلفاً لجماعة من تقدمه من العباد المجتهدين والزهاد القانعين ، سمع بنيسابور أبا محمد يحيى بن منصور القاضى وأبا عمرو بن نجيدو أبا على الرفاء الهروى وأبا أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النسائى وأقرانهم ، وتفقه للشافعي على أبي الحسن الماسرجسى وسمع بالعراق بعد التسعين والثلاثمائة ثم خرج إلى الحجاز وجاوز حرم الله وأمنه مكة وصحب بها العباد الصالحين وسمع الحديث من أهلها والواردين وانصرف إلى وطنه بنيسابور وقد أنجز الله له موعوده على لسان نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( في حديث سهيل عن أبيه عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الله تعالى إذا أحب عبداً نادى جبريل أن الله قد أحب فلاناً فأحبه فينادي جبريل بذلك في السماء فيحبه أهل السماء ثم يوضع له القبول في الأرض ) فلزم منزله ومجلسه وبذل النفس والمال والجاه للمستوردين من الغرباء والفقراء المنقطع بهم حتى صار الفقراء في مجالسه كما حدثونا عن إبراهيم بن الحسين ثنا عمرو بن عون قال ثنا يحيى ابن اليمان قال كان الفقراء في مجلس سفيان كأمراء ، قد وفقه الله تعالى لعمارة المساجد والحياض والقناطر والدروب وكسوة الفقراء العراة من الغرباء والبلدية حتى بنى دارا للمرضى بعد أن خربت الدور القديمة لهم بنيسابور ووكل جماعة من أصحابه المستورين بتمريضهم وحمل مياههم إلى الأطباء ، وشراء الأدوية. ولقد أخبرني الثقة أن الله تعالى ذكره قد شفى جماعة منهم فكساهم وزودهم إلى الرجوع إلى أوطانهم وقد صنف في علوم الشريعة ودلائل النبوة وفي سير العباد والزهاد كتبا نسخها جماعة من أهل الحديث وسمعوها منه وسارت تلك المصنفات في بلاد المسلمين تاريخا لنيسابور وعلمائها الماضين منهم والباقين وكثيرا أقول أن لا يباهي بأجمع منه علما وزهدا وتواضعاً وإرشاداً إلى الله تعالى ذكره وإلى شريعة نبيه المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى آله وإلى الزاهدين في الدنيا الفانية والتزود منها للآخرة الباقية ، زاده الله توفيقاً وأسعدنا بأيامه ووفقنا للشكر الله تعالى ذكره بمكانه أنه خير معين و موفق .
وقد روى عنه الحاكم وهو أسند منه
أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن على بن أحمد الغساني بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد الشيباني ببغداد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد ابن علی ثابت الخطيب : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان واسم أبي عثمان محمد ابن إبراهيم ويكنى عبد الملك أبا سعد الواعظ من أهل نيسابور قدم بغداد حاجا وحدث بها عن يحيى بن منصور القاضي وحامد بن محمد الهروي ومحمد بن الحسن بن إسماعيل السراج وأبي عمرو بن مطر وإسماعيل بن نجيد وأبى أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النيسابوريين ومحمد بن عبد
And among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman al-Naysaburi al-Kharkushi al-Zahid (may God have mercy on him). I read to the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Shihami from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi, who said: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abd al-Malik ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Uthman, the preacher and ascetic, studied jurisprudence in his youth, became ascetic, and associated with ascetics and devotees until God made him a successor to a group of preceding devout worshippers and contented ascetics. He heard (hadith) in Nishapur from Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Abu Amr ibn Najid, Abu Ali al-Rifa' al-Harawi, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Nasa'i, and their peers. He studied Shafi'i jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi and heard hadith in Iraq after 390 AH. Then he traveled to the Hijaz and entered the sacred sanctuary of God and its security, Mecca. There he accompanied righteous worshippers and heard hadith from its people and visitors. He returned to his homeland, Nishapur, and God fulfilled for him His promise on the tongue of His chosen Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Suhayl from his father from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When God loves a servant, He calls Jibril: God loves so-and-so, so love him. Then Jibril calls out in the heavens, and the inhabitants of the heavens love him, then acceptance is placed for him on earth.' So he stuck to his home and his gathering, and he devoted his soul, wealth, and status to those who came to him from strangers and the poor who were stranded, until the poor in his gatherings were like princes, as they narrated to us from Ibrahim ibn al-Husayn: Amr ibn Awn told us: Yahya ibn al-Yaman told us: The poor in the gathering of Sufyan were like princes. God facilitated for him the building of mosques, cisterns, bridges, and roads, and clothing the naked poor from strangers and locals, until he built a house for the sick after the old houses for them in Nishapur had fallen into ruin. He appointed a group of his trustworthy companions to nurse them, carry their water to the doctors, and buy medicines. A trustworthy person told me that God cured a group of them, so he clothed them and provided them with provisions until they returned to their homelands. He authored books on the sciences of the Sharia, proofs of prophethood, and the biographies of worshippers and ascetics. A group of hadith scholars copied them and heard them from him, and those works spread throughout the lands of the Muslims, a history of Nishapur and its past and present scholars. And I say much: that no one comparable to him can be found in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance to God and to the Sharia of His chosen Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) and to the ascetics in the fleeting world and taking provision from it for the eternal afterlife. May God increase him in success, make us happy through his days, and grant us gratitude to God for his station, for He is the best Helper and Grantor of success. 
And al-Hakim narrated from him, and he is more reliable than him (or: he is a higher authority). The two shaykhs, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani in Baghdad, told us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali Thabit al-Khatib told us: Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Uthman – and the name of Abi Uthman is Muhammad ibn Ibrahim – and he is called Abd al-Malik Abu Sa'd the preacher, from the people of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad as a pilgrim and narrated there from Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Isma'il al-Sarraj, Abu Amr ibn Matar, Isma'il ibn Najid, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Naysaburiyyun, and Muhammad ibn Abd...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biography of the ascetic and scholar Abu Sa'd al-Kharkushi. It begins by introducing his full name and his ascetic character. It then describes his early study of fiqh and his association with ascetics. He studied under prominent teachers in Nishapur and Iraq, and later traveled to Mecca, where he accompanied righteous worshippers. The biography emphasizes that God fulfilled for him a promise from the hadith of Suhayl, which narrates that when God loves a servant, He commands Jibril to love him, leading to acceptance on earth. 
After returning to Nishapur, Abu Sa'd devoted himself to charity: he spent his wealth on the poor and strangers, building mosques, cisterns, bridges, and even a hospital for the sick. He personally arranged for nursing and medicines. The text notes that many were healed and sent back to their homelands. 
He also authored books on Islamic sciences, proofs of prophethood, and biographies of ascetics. His works became widely known. The author praises him as unparalleled in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance. 
Finally, another chain of transmission confirms his name and his hadith narrations, listing several of his teachers. The passage ends abruptly with 'Muhammad ibn Abd' as the page ends.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith about God's love implies predestination — that if God loves someone, they have no free will.
Correction: The hadith describes the effects of God's love, not a deterministic compulsion. It emphasizes that divine love leads to acceptance on earth, inspiring action as seen in al-Kharkushi's life.

The Integrated Asceticism of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid
Multiple narratives detailing the life, virtues, and works of the ascetic scholar Abu Sa'd al-Zahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholar 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi combined deep piety, active charity, and lawful earning, redefining asceticism as social engagement.

Core Idea
True asceticism is not isolation but service to others while earning lawful livelihood.

This lesson presents the biography of a remarkable scholar who balanced inner piety with outward service. Through multiple accounts, we see how his love for Allah translated into building hospitals, teaching, and earning his own bread by making caps. The passage challenges the notion that asceticism means withdrawing from society, offering instead a model of engaged spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening hadith on divine love
Start with the hadith about Allah loving a servant. Notice how it sets the spiritual foundation for the entire biography: the scholar's actions flow from being loved by Allah.
This hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Bukhari.
2
Examine his charitable works
Identify the various projects he undertook: building mosques, water basins, bridges, and a hospital. Note how he organized nursing and medicine procurement.
His charity extended to strangers and locals alike.
3
Review his scholarly contributions
He authored books on Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and biographies of ascetics. These works spread widely and served as a history of Nishapur.
He also built a school and a library.
4
Understand his personal lifestyle and death
He worked as a cap-maker to earn a lawful living, avoiding dependency. The biographical notices confirm his trustworthiness and give his death year. The rain prayer anecdote shows his spiritual station.
His death is recorded as 400 AH or 406 AH depending on the source.

ذكره بمكانه أنه خير معين و موفق . وقد روى عنه الحاكم وهو أسند منه أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن على بن أحمد الغساني بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد الشيباني ببغداد قالا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد ابن علی ثابت الخطيب : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان واسم أبي عثمان محمد ابن إبراهيم ويكنى عبد الملك أبا سعد الواعظ من أهل نيسابور قدم بغداد حاجا وحدث بها عن يحيى بن منصور القاضي وحامد بن محمد الهروي ومحمد بن الحسن بن إسماعيل السراج وأبي عمرو بن مطر وإسماعيل بن نجيد وأبى أحمد محمد بن محمد بن الحسن النيسابوريين ومحمد بن عبد الله بن بن جبير النسوى وبشر بن أحمد الاسفراينى وعلى بن بندار ابن الحسن الصوفي وأبى إسحق المزكى وأبى سهل الصعلوكي حدثنا عنه أبو محمد الخلال والأزهرى وعبد العزيز الأزجى والتنوخي وقال لى التنوخي قدم علينا أبو سعد الزاهد بغداد حاجا في سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثماية وخرج إلى مكة فأقام بها مجاوراً قال أبو بكر الخطيب وكان ثقة صالحاً ورعاً زاد أبو منصور زاهدا ، سألت أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك النيسابورى عن وفاة أبي سعد فقال فى سنة ست وأربعمائة . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل إجازة قال : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان محمد بن إبراهيم النيسابوري أبو سعد الزاهد الخركوشى الواعظ الأستاذ الكامل أحد أفراد خراسان علماً وزهداً وورعاً وخشية وطريقة ، تفقه على أبى الحسن الماسرجسى ثم ترك الجاه وجالس الزهاد ولزم العمل وحج وجاور ثم رجع إلى خراسان وكان يعمل القلانس ويأمر ببيعها بحيث لا يدرى أنها من صنعته ويأكل من كسب يده وبنى في سكته المدرسة ودار المرضى ووقف أوقافاً عليها ووضع في المدرسة خزانة للكتب وصنف أعداداً من الكتب وتوفى فى جمادى الأولى سنة وأربعمائة . وقال عبد الغافر سمعت أبا الفضل محمد بن عبد الله الصرام الزاهد يقول رأيت الأستاذ يستسقى ويقول : الترب . إليك جئنا وأنت جئت بنا ولیس رب سواك يغنينا بابك رحب فناؤه کرم تؤوى إلى بابك المساكينا سبع ثم يدعو ويقول : اللهم اسقنا قال فما اتم ثلاثاً حتى سقينا كأفواه سبع
Suhayl from his father from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that Allah Almighty when He loves a servant calls Gabriel: 'Allah loves so-and-so, so love him.' Gabriel then calls out in heaven, and the inhabitants of heaven love him, then acceptance is placed for him on the earth. So he kept to his home and his gathering, and devoted his soul, wealth, and status to those who came from among the strangers and the poor who were cut off, until the poor in his gatherings became like princes, as they narrated to us from Ibrahim ibn al-Husayn who said: 'Amr ibn 'Awn narrated to us: Yahya ibn al-Yaman said: The poor in Sufyan's gathering were like princes.' Allah had granted him success in building mosques, water basins, bridges, and roads, and clothing the naked poor from among the strangers and locals, until he built a house for the sick after the old houses for them in Nishapur had fallen into ruin, and he appointed a group of his trustworthy companions to nurse them, carry their water to the physicians, and purchase medicines. A trustworthy person informed me that Allah (mentioned) cured a group of them, so he clothed them and provided them with provisions until they returned to their homelands. He authored books on the sciences of the Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and the biographies of worshippers and ascetics; a group of hadith scholars copied them and heard them from him, and those works spread throughout the lands of the Muslims, a history of Nishapur and its scholars, past and present. I say much that no one can boast of a more complete person than him in knowledge, asceticism, humility, and guidance to Allah (mentioned) and to the Shari'a of His Chosen Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) and to the ascetics in the fleeting world and provision from it for the lasting Hereafter. May Allah increase him in success, make us happy with his days, and grant us gratitude to Allah (mentioned) for his sake; He is the best Helper and Giver of success. Al-Hakim narrated from him, and he is more reliable than him. The two shaykhs Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Shaybani in Baghdad informed us, both saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali Thabit al-Khatib said: 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman (the name of Abu 'Uthman is Muhammad ibn Ibrahim), and 'Abd al-Malik is known as Abu Sa'd al-Wa'iz from Nishapur. He came to Baghdad for pilgrimage and narrated there from Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi, Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Isma'il al-Sarraj, Abu 'Amr ibn Matar, Isma'il ibn Najid, Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Naysaburi, Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Jubayr al-Nasawi, Bishr ibn Ahmad al-Isfarayini, 'Ali ibn Bandar ibn al-Hasan al-Sufi, Abu Ishaq al-Muzakki, and Abu Sahl al-Sa'luqi. He was narrated from by Abu Muhammad al-Khallal, al-Azhari, 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Azaji, and al-Tanukhi. Al-Tanukhi said: Abu Sa'd al-Zahid came to us in Baghdad for pilgrimage in the year 393 AH and went to Mecca and stayed there as a neighbor. Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: He was trustworthy, righteous, and pious. Abu Mansur added: An ascetic. I asked Abu Salih Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi about the death of Abu Sa'd, and he said: In the year 406 AH. The shaykh Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us by permission, saying: 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburi, Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi al-Wa'iz, the perfect master, one of the unique individuals of Khurasan in knowledge, asceticism, piety, fear, and way. He studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then abandoned status and sat with the ascetics, adhered to action, performed pilgrimage, and stayed (in Mecca), then returned to Khurasan. He used to make caps and order them sold without it being known that they were his work, and he ate from the earnings of his own hands. He built a school and a hospital in his alley, endowed endowments for them, placed a library of books in the school, and authored many books. He died in Jumada al-Ula of the year 400 AH. 'Abd al-Ghafir said: I heard Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Siram al-Zahid say: I saw the master praying for rain and saying: 'The dust. To You we have come, and You have brought us, and there is no Lord besides You to enrich us. Your door is wide, its courtyard is generous, the poor are sheltered at Your door.' Seven. Then he would supplicate and say: 'O Allah, give us rain.' He said: He did not complete it three times until we were given rain like the mouths of seven.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a composite biographical entry for the scholar 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi 'Uthman al-Naysaburi (Abu Sa'd al-Zahid). It begins with a hadith about divine love for a servant, which sets a spiritual tone, and then applies it to the subject: because God loved him, he was devoted to serving the poor and strangers. The narrative proceeds chronologically: his charitable works (building mosques, bridges, a hospital), his authorship of books on Shari'a, proofs of prophethood, and ascetic biographies, and his widespread reputation. Then follows a formal biographical notice from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, listing his teachers, his pilgrimage visits, and his death date. A third account from 'Abd al-Ghafir adds details about his ascetic practice: he worked as a cap-maker to earn a lawful living, built a school and hospital, endowed them, and left many authored works. The entry closes with an anecdote of his prayer for rain, with a poetic supplication, showing his spiritual station.

Key Terms
عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان
أبو سعد الزاهد
الخركوشى
نيسابور
صاحب التصانيف
القلانس
دار المرضى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Asceticism means withdrawing from society and avoiding all worldly involvement.
Correction: This biography shows a model of asceticism that includes active social service, building hospitals and schools, teaching, and earning a lawful living through manual labor.

Checkpoint
What did 'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi do to earn a lawful living according to the biography?
A) He worked as a farmer.
B) He made caps and sold them anonymously.
C) He relied on endowments.
D) He taught for a salary.

Key Takeaway
'Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi embodied an asceticism that was not withdrawal but active engagement in society, building institutions, teaching, and earning his own lawful livelihood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd made caps and sold them without anyone knowing. What is one good deed you have done that no one knows about—and if you have none, what is stopping you from starting today?
?
He built a hospital, a school, endowed them, and wrote books. If you were to die tonight, what tangible, lasting contribution would you leave behind for the Ummah? Be honest.
?
When he prayed for rain, it poured. Is your dua so weak because your heart is still attached to the world? What one attachment must you break so that your words carry weight with Allah?

Beginning of al-Bistami's Biography
Ibn 'Asakir begins the biographical entry for al-Bistami with name, titles, and isnad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn 'Asakir introduces the scholar Muhammad al-Bistami, identifying his titles and the chain of transmission used to authenticate his biography.

Core Idea
Ibn 'Asakir establishes al-Bistami's scholarly credentials through his lineage and isnad.

This passage opens the biography of the jurist-theologian Muhammad al-Bistami. Ibn 'Asakir provides his full name and honorary titles, then traces the chain of transmission through which he received his knowledge. The entry sets the stage for al-Bistami's scholarly credentials and connections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the phrase 'Among them' at the start, linking to previous entries.
2
Identify the titles given to al-Bistami
List the titles mentioned: judge (قاضي), jurist (فقيه), theologian (متكلم), preacher (واعظ). What does each title suggest about his role?
The word 'البارغ' is unclear; possibly a place name or descriptor.
3
Trace the chain of transmission
Identify the narrators: al-Bistami wrote to al-Qushayri, who heard from al-Bayhaqi, who heard from al-Hakim. This isnad authenticates the information about al-Bistami.
This chain shows the care in preserving scholarly heritage.

ومنهم القاضي أبو عمر محمد بن الحسين البسطامی رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ الإمام أبو نصر القشيري قال أنا أبو بكر البيهقى قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ الحاكم قال : محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن يحيى الفقيه المتكلم البارغ الواعظ أبو عمر بن أبي سعد البسطامي سمع باصبهان أبا القسم سليمان بن أحمد اللخمي وأقرانه
And among them is the judge Abu 'Umar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to the shaykh Imam Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, saying: Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi informed us, saying: Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz al-Hakim informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya, the jurist, theologian, al-Barigh (?), preacher, Abu 'Umar ibn Abi Sa'd al-Bistami, heard in Isfahan from Abu al-Qasim Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Lakhmi and his peers.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage begins a new biographical entry in the chain. The phrase 'among them' links it to the previous list of scholars. The entry gives the name and titles of Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, noting his roles as judge (قاضي), jurist (فقيه), theologian (متكلم), and preacher (واعظ). It provides the chain of transmission for the information: via a letter to al-Qushayri from al-Bayhaqi, who heard from al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. The entry is cut off at the mention of his teachers in Isfahan. The fragment thus serves as an introduction to the scholar's identity and his educational credentials.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This isnad connects al-Bistami to giants like al-Qushayri and al-Bayhaqi. Who are the living teachers connecting you to the prophetic inheritance? Have you ever written down your own chain of teachers? If not, what is stopping you from doing it this week?
?
Al-Bistami is described as both a jurist (فقيه) and a theologian (متكلم). Which of these two dimensions of knowledge is weaker in your own life? What concrete step will you take this month to strengthen it?
?
The passage ends by stating that al-Bistami ‘heard from’ certain scholars. Hearing is a passive act, but it implies seeking. When did you last actively seek out a teacher to hear sacred knowledge from, rather than just reading online? If you cannot recall, what will you do to change that?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Biography of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi
Ibn Asakir compiles two reports on Abu Sa'd al-Zahid's life and miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and spiritual station of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, a renowned ascetic and scholar of Khurasan, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Zahid embodied knowledge, asceticism, and answered prayers.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents two reports on the life of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi. The first provides key dates of his pilgrimage and death; the second details his piety, self-sufficiency, charitable works, and a miraculous rain prayer. Together, they paint a portrait of a scholar who fully practiced what he preached.

Guided Path
1
Read the two reports
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the different chains of transmission (al-Tanukhi and Abd al-Ghafir) and how each report adds unique information.
The passage is a compilation of two separate accounts.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the important facts: his pilgrimage in 393 AH, his death around 406 AH, his teacher Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, his trade as a cap-maker, and his founding of a school and hospital.
Pay attention to the clarity of the death year between the two reports.
3
Reflect on the rain prayer anecdote
Read the story of his prayer for rain. Consider what it reveals about his spiritual rank and the acceptance of his supplication.
This anecdote demonstrates his closeness to Allah.
4
Resolve the death year ambiguity
The second report says 'sana wa arba'ami'a' (year 400-something). Compare with the first report's clear '406 AH' to understand the intended meaning.
The phrase likely means 'the year 400-something', and the first report specifies 406.

الله بن بن جبير النسوى وبشر بن أحمد الاسفراينى وعلى بن بندار ابن الحسن الصوفي وأبى إسحق المزكى وأبى سهل الصعلوكي حدثنا عنه أبو محمد الخلال والأزهرى وعبد العزيز الأزجى والتنوخي وقال لى التنوخي قدم علينا أبو سعد الزاهد بغداد حاجا في سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثماية وخرج إلى مكة فأقام بها مجاوراً قال أبو بكر الخطيب وكان ثقة صالحاً ورعاً زاد أبو منصور زاهدا ، سألت أبا صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك النيسابورى عن وفاة أبي سعد فقال فى سنة ست وأربعمائة . • أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل إجازة قال : عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان محمد بن إبراهيم النيسابوري أبو سعد الزاهد الخركوشى الواعظ الأستاذ الكامل أحد أفراد خراسان علماً وزهداً وورعاً وخشية وطريقة ، تفقه على أبى الحسن الماسرجسى ثم ترك الجاه وجالس الزهاد ولزم العمل وحج وجاور ثم رجع إلى خراسان وكان يعمل القلانس ويأمر ببيعها بحيث لا يدرى أنها من صنعته ويأكل من كسب يده وبنى في سكته المدرسة ودار المرضى ووقف أوقافاً عليها ووضع في المدرسة خزانة للكتب وصنف أعداداً من الكتب وتوفى فى جمادى الأولى سنة وأربعمائة . وقال عبد الغافر سمعت أبا الفضل محمد بن عبد الله الصرام الزاهد يقول رأيت الأستاذ يستسقى ويقول : الترب . إليك جئنا وأنت جئت بنا ولیس رب سواك يغنينا بابك رحب فناؤه كرم تؤوى إلى بابك المساكينا ثم يدعو ويقول : اللهم اسقنا قال فما اتم ثلاثاً حتى سقينا كأفواه السبع
Allah ibn ibn Jubayr al-Nasawi and Bishr ibn Ahmad al-Isfara'ini and Ali ibn Bandar ibn al-Hasan al-Sufi and Abu Ishaq al-Muzakki and Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki — Abu Muhammad al-Khallal and al-Azhari and Abd al-Aziz al-Azji and al-Tanukhi narrated from him. And al-Tanukhi said to me: Abu Sa'd al-Zahid came to us in Baghdad as a pilgrim in the year 393 AH, and he left to Mecca and resided there as a neighbor. Abu Bakr al-Khatib said: He was trustworthy, righteous, devout — Abu Mansur added: ascetic. I asked Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Naysaburi about the death of Abu Sa'd, and he said: In the year 406 AH. • The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il informed us by permission, saying: Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Uthman Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburi, Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, the preacher, the complete master, one of the unique individuals of Khurasan in knowledge, asceticism, piety, fear, and way. He studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then he abandoned status and sat with ascetics, adhered to action, performed pilgrimage, resided, then returned to Khurasan. He used to make caps and order them to be sold such that it was not known they were his handiwork, and he ate from the earnings of his hands. He built in his lane a school and a hospital, endowed properties for them, placed in the school a library of books, and authored numerous books. He died in Jumada al-Ula of the year 400-something AH. And Abd al-Ghafir said: I heard Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Siram al-Zahid say: I saw the master praying for rain, saying: 'O dust! To You we have come, and You have brought us; no lord besides You suffices us. Your gate is spacious, its courtyard is generous; the poor are sheltered at Your gate.' Then he supplicated and said: 'O Allah, give us rain.' He said: He did not complete three times until we were watered like mouths of seven.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry comprising two separate reports on the life of Abu Sa'd al-Zahid al-Kharkushi, a famous ascetic and scholar of Khurasan. The first report, transmitted by al-Tanukhi via a chain that includes several narrators, notes that Abu Sa'd visited Baghdad as a pilgrim in 393 AH, then went to Mecca and resided there. Al-Khatib confirms his trustworthiness and piety, and his death year is reported as 406 AH. The second report, from Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il, provides more detail: Abu Sa'd studied jurisprudence under Abu al-Hasan al-Masarjisi, then abandoned worldly status to sit with ascetics. He was a cap-maker and sold his own work anonymously to eat from his own earnings. He built a school and a hospital, endowed them, and stocked the school with books. He wrote many books and died in Jumada al-Ula of 400 AH (the exact decade is ambiguous: 'sana wa arba'ami'a' likely means 400-something, but the earlier report specifies 406). The passage concludes with an anecdote: he prayed for rain with a poem and supplication, and rain came immediately. This illustrates his spiritual station and the acceptance of his prayers.

عبد الملك بن أبي عثمان
القلانس
المدرسة
دار المرضى
الاستسقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'سنة وأربعمائة' in the second report is interpreted as exactly 400 AH.
Correction: The first report clarifies that 'سنة وأربعمائة' means 'the year 400-something' (i.e., 406 AH), not precisely 400.

Checkpoint
In which year did Abu Sa'd al-Zahid die according to the first report?
A) 393 AH
B) 400 AH
C) 406 AH
D) 410 AH

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Zahid was a scholar-ascetic whose life exemplified self-reliance, charity, and spiritual authority, as evidenced by his answered prayer for rain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd abandoned his pursuit of status and fame to sit with ascetics. What is one status or position in your life that you cling to, and how can you begin to detach from it this week?
?
He made caps and sold them anonymously so that no one would know they were his handiwork. In what areas of your life do you seek recognition, and can you perform one act of charity or service this week without letting anyone know it was you?
?
When he prayed for rain, he turned to Allah with humility and a poem acknowledging his need. In your current trials, do you turn to Allah with the same desperate reliance, or do you rely on your own resources? What is one specific thing you can only ask from Allah?

The Travels and Appointment of al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami
Ibn Asakir details his teachers, travels, and judgeship charter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life, scholarly travels, and the event of his appointment as judge of Nishapur.

Core Idea
A judge's journey from student to courtroom begins with travel and a royal charter.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to a key Shafi'i figure, al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami. Through a chain of narrators, we learn of his extensive travels in search of knowledge and his formal appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about his travels and appointment
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of narrators (isnad) that introduces the information.
This is a typical biographical entry in a historical work.
2
Identify the places he studied
The passage lists several cities where Abu 'Umar heard hadith: Isfahan, Iraq, Basra, and Ahwaz. Locate each in the text.
These travels show his dedication to gathering knowledge.
3
Note the date and manner of his appointment
The charter for the judgeship of Nishapur arrived on Thursday, 3rd Dhu al-Qa'dah 388 AH. He was seated in the Mosque of Raja. Mark the significance of this date.
The joy of the hadith scholars indicates his respected status.
4
Understand the reaction of the scholars
The people of hadith showed immense joy, scattering gifts. The author mentions writing thanks to the Sultan. Reflect on the communal celebration.
This highlights the importance of judicial appointments in that era.

ومنهم القاضي أبو عمر محمد بن الحسين البسطامی رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ الإمام أبو نصر القشيري قال أنا أبو بكر البيهقى قال أخبرنا أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الحافظ الحاكم قال : محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن يحيى الفقيه المتكلم البارغ الواعظ أبو عمر بن أبي سعد البسطامي سمع باصبهان أبا القسم سليمان بن أحمد اللخمي وأقرانه وبالعراق أبا بكر بن مالك وأبا محمد بن ماسى وأقرانهما وسمع بالبصرة والأهواز وورد له العهد بقضاء نيسابور وقرئ علينا العهد غداة الخميس الثالث من ذي القعدة سنة ثمان وثمانين وثلاثمائة وأجلسه في مجلس القضاء في مسجد رجا في تلك الساعة وأظهر أهل الحديث من الفرح والاستبشار والنثار ما يطول شرحه وكتبنا بالدعاء والشكر إلى السلطان أيده الله وإلى أوليائه حدثني الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسي بدمشق عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر بن أبي بكر قال قال أبو علي الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر الأستاذ أبي عثمان إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن الصابونى قال وذكر القاضي أبا عمر البسطامي فقال كان منفرداً بلطائف السيادة معتمداً لمواقف الوفادة سفر بين السلطان المعظم وبين مجلس الخلافة أيام القادر بالله فافتن أهل بغداد بلسانه وإحسانه ويزهم في إيراده وإصداره بصحة إتقانه ونكث في ذلك المشهد النبوى . والمحفل الأمامي أشياء أعجب بها كفاته وسلم الفضل له فيها حماته وقالوا مثله فليكن نائباً عن ذلك السلطان المؤيد بالتوفيق والنصرة وافداً على مثل هذه الحضرة حتى صدر وحقائبه مملوءة من أصناف الإكرام وسهامه فائزة بأقصى المرام ثم كان شافعى العلم شريحى الحكم سحبانی البیان سحار اللسان أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم بن العباس والـفـقـيـه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : محمد ابن الحسين ابن محمد بن الهيثم أبو عمر البسطامي الواعظ الفقيه على مذهب الشافعي ولی قضاء نيسابور وقدم بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن عبد الرحمن ابن الجارود الرقى وسليمان بن أحمد الطبراني وأبي بكر القباب الأصبهاني وأحمد بن محمود بن خرزاد الأهوازى حدثني عنه الحسن بن محمد الخلال وذكر لى أنه قدم بغداد في حياة أبي حامد الاسفراینی قال وكان إماماً نظاراً وكان أبو حامد يعظمه ويحله
And among them is the judge Abu 'Umar Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to the Imam Abu Nasr al-Qushayri, saying: Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi told us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Hafiz al-Hakim informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya, the jurist, the theologian, the brilliant, the preacher, Abu 'Umar ibn Abi Sa'd al-Bistami. He heard in Isfahan from Abu al-Qasim Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Lakhmi and his peers, and in Iraq from Abu Bakr ibn Malik and Abu Muhammad ibn Masi and their peers, and he heard in Basra and Ahwaz. The charter for the judgeship of Nishapur arrived for him, and the charter was read to us on the morning of Thursday, the third of Dhu al-Qa'dah of the year 388 AH. He was seated in the council of judgment in the Mosque of Raja at that hour, and the people of hadith showed joy, gladness, and scattering that would take long to describe. We wrote with supplication and thanks to the Sultan, may Allah support him, and to his clients. The Shaykh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salamasi narrated to me in Damascus from his father, the judge Abu Tahir ibn Abi Bakr, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Marandi, the jurist, said in mentioning the master Abu Uthman Isma'il ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni: He mentioned the judge Abu 'Umar al-Bistami and said: He was unique in the subtleties of leadership, relying on the stations of deputation. He traveled between the exalted Sultan and the council of the Caliphate during the days of al-Qadir bi'llah. The people of Baghdad were captivated by his tongue and his beneficence, and he excelled in his presentations and dispatches with the correctness of his proficiency. He broke in that prophetic assembly and the imam's gathering things that amazed his peers, and his protectors conceded excellence to him, and they said: 'Might such a one be a deputy for that Sultan, supported by divine guidance and victory, an envoy to such a presence.' Until he issued forth, his baggage filled with varieties of honor, and his arrows winning the utmost goal. Then he was Shafi'i in knowledge, Shurayhi in judgment, Sahbani in eloquence, enchanting of tongue. The noble Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Abbas and the jurist Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham Abu 'Umar al-Bistami, the preacher, the jurist according to the Shafi'i school, was appointed to the judgeship of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad and narrated there from Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Jarud al-Raqqi, Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Tabarani, Abu Bakr al-Qabad al-Isbahani, and Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Khurzadh al-Ahwazi. Al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Khallal narrated to me from him, and he mentioned that he came to Baghdad during the lifetime of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. He said: He was a leading scholar of kalam, and Abu Hamid used to venerate and honor him.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a composite biographical entry for al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami, a Shafi'i jurist, theologian, and preacher. It is presented through multiple chains of transmission. The first chain goes through al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim, stating that Abu 'Umar studied in Isfahan, Iraq, Basra, and Ahwaz. His appointment as judge of Nishapur occurred in 388 AH, and the reading of the charter was a joyous event. The second chain, via al-Salamasi, quotes a description of Abu 'Umar's role as an envoy between the Sultan and the Caliph al-Qadir bi'llah, emphasizing his eloquence and diplomatic skill. The description likens him to Shurayh in judgment and Sahban in eloquence, and notes that he was a Shafi'i in fiqh. The final chain, via al-Khatib, confirms his Shafi'i adherence, his teachers, and his visit to Baghdad during the time of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, who held him in high esteem. The passage thus presents Abu 'Umar as a man of multiple talents: judge, preacher, envoy, and theologian.

Key Terms
القاضي أبو عمر البسطامي
محمد بن الحسين
قضاء نيسابور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'البارغ' means 'the arrow'.
Correction: It is likely a misspelling of 'البارع' meaning 'the brilliant', which fits the context of describing his scholarly abilities.

Checkpoint
In which year was Abu 'Umar al-Bistami appointed judge of Nishapur according to the text?
A) 388 AH
B) 393 AH
C) 400 AH
D) 406 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami was a well-traveled scholar appointed as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, bringing joy to the hadith scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read about al-Bistami's extensive travels to learn from various teachers. Where are you in your own journey of seeking knowledge? Have you sacrificed comfort to learn from those who carry authentic knowledge, or are you content with what is easy? What step will you take this week to prioritize seeking beneficial knowledge over your current routine?
?
The people of hadith rejoiced at the appointment of a righteous judge. When was the last time you felt genuine joy at seeing a person of faith placed in a position of authority? Does your heart celebrate the rise of the pious, or are you indifferent? Ask yourself: if a scholar you respect were appointed as a leader tomorrow, would you respond with the same exuberance as the hadith scholars of Nishapur?
?
Consider the chain of narrators in this lesson: it took multiple trustworthy individuals to transmit this single account to us. Your faith today is built on the sacrifices of scholars who traveled, verified, and taught. How does this realization affect your relationship with the knowledge you have? Do you treat it as a trust (amana) to pass on, or as a collection of facts? Write down one concrete way you will honor these transmitters by sharing what you learn.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Eloquence and Diplomatic Role of al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami
The author describes his role as envoy and his scholarly attributes through multiple chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu 'Umar al-Bistami served as an envoy between the Sultan and the Caliph, and his reputation for eloquence and knowledge.

Core Idea
A judge's tongue can move between sultan and caliph, captivating all with his speech.

The second part of Ibn Asakir's biography shifts from his appointment to a vivid description of Abu 'Umar's role as a diplomat. Through a chain of reporters, including a jurist's tribute, we see him as a unique figure who could represent the Sultan before the Caliph, and whose eloquence was compared to legendary figures.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of his diplomatic role
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the chain of narrators (isnad) that brings the description.
This part comes from a different narrator than the first.
2
Notice the phrases praising his eloquence
The description uses terms like 'Sahbani al-bayan', 'Shuraihi al-hukm', and 'sahhar al-lisan'. Understand these as high praise for his speech and judgment.
Sahban was famous for eloquence; Shurayh for judicial wisdom.
3
Understand the context of his diplomatic mission
He traveled between the Sultan and the Caliph al-Qadir bi'llah, captivating Baghdad with his tongue and beneficence.
He returned with honors and his arrows hitting the mark.
4
Recognize the high regard of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini
The final chain confirms his Shafi'i school and that Abu Hamid, a leading scholar, venerated him.
This shows his high status among contemporary scholars.

Commentary
This passage is a composite biographical entry for al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami, a Shafi'i jurist, theologian, and preacher. It is presented through multiple chains of transmission. The first chain goes through al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim, stating that Abu 'Umar studied in Isfahan, Iraq, Basra, and Ahwaz. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'سحار اللسان' means 'magician of the tongue' in a negative sense.
Correction: It is a metaphor for extreme eloquence and persuasiveness, not literal magic.

Al-Qadi Abu 'Umar al-Bistami was not only a judge but also a gifted diplomat and eloquent speaker, recognized by both the Sultan and the Caliph.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have a tongue that can captivate, just as Abu 'Umar did. Are you using your words to build bridges of understanding and mercy, or are you using them to tear down? Today, commit to speaking one specific word of encouragement to someone you have avoided.
?
Abu 'Umar was a judge, a scholar, and a diplomat—he used his positions to serve both the rulers and the community. Examine your own roles in life: are you serving Allah's creation with excellence, or are you merely going through the motions? Write down one concrete act of service you will perform this week that goes beyond your usual duties.
?
The great scholar Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini venerated Abu 'Umar. Whom do you honor in your life? Are you actively learning from those who embody knowledge and character? Identify one trait of Abu 'Umar—like his eloquence, fairness, or diplomatic skill—and describe one practical step you will take this week to cultivate that trait.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami through multiple chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami as recorded by Ibn Asakir, including his appointment as judge, his scholarly status, and his connections.

Core Idea
Abu Umar al-Bastami was a Shafi'i judge and scholar who bridged the worlds of hadith, fiqh, and diplomacy.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari presents a multi-sourced biography of Abu Umar al-Bastami, a prominent Shafi'i judge and preacher. Through several chains of narration, we learn about his appointment as Qadi of Nishapur, his eloquence and diplomatic missions, his veneration by leading scholars like Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, and the various reports of his death. The entry exemplifies how classical biographers compiled information from multiple eyewitnesses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage overview
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the biographical flow. Note the different sections introduced by different chains.
The passage contains multiple isnads, so look for phrases like 'حدثني', 'أخبرنا', etc.
2
Focus on the appointment report
Notice the detailed description of his appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, including the date, location, and the joy of the hadith scholars.
This is a vivid historical account showing the public celebration.
3
Examine the praise from contemporaries
Read the laudatory description that praises his eloquence, judgment, and diplomatic role. Notice the similes: 'Shafi'i in knowledge, Shurayhi in judgment, Sahbani in eloquence'.
These comparisons highlight his excellence in multiple fields.
4
Analyze the scholarly details and death reports
Review the information from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi about his teachers, his veneration by Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini, and the two death dates (407 and 408 AH). Note his sons al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad.
The multiple death reports show the diversity of sources.

وبالعراق أبا بكر بن مالك وأبا محمد بن ماسى وأقرانهما وسمع بالبصرة والأهواز وورد له العهد بقضاء نيسابور وقرئ علينا العهد غداة الخميس الثالث من ذي القعدة سنة ثمان وثمانين وثلاثمائة وأجلسه في مجلس القضاء في مسجد رجا في تلك الساعة وأظهر أهل الحديث من الفرح والاستبشار والنثار ما يطول شرحه وكتبنا بالدعاء والشكر إلى السلطان أيده الله وإلى أوليائه حدثني الشيخ أبو بكر يحيى بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن محمد السلماسي بدمشق عن أبيه القاضي أبي طاهر بن أبي بكر قال قال أبو علي الحسن بن نصر بن كاكا المرندى الفقيه في ذكر الأستاذ أبي عثمان إسماعيل بن عبد الرحمن الصابونى قال وذكر القاضي أبا عمر البسطامي فقال كان منفرداً بلطائف السيادة معتمداً لمواقف الوفادة سفر بين السلطان المعظم وبين مجلس الخلافة أيام القادر بالله فافتن أهل بغداد بلسانه وإحسانه ويزهم في إيراده وإصداره بصحة إتقانه ونكث في ذلك المشهد النبوي والمحفل الأمامي أشياء أعجب بها كفاته وسلم الفضل له فيها حماته وقالوا مثله فليكن نائباً عن ذلك السلطان المؤيد بالتوفيق والنصرة وافداً على مثل هذه الحضرة حتى صدر وحقائبه مملوءة من أصناف الإكرام وسهامه فائزة بأقصى المرام ثم كان شافعى العلم شريحى الحكم سحبانى البيان سحار اللسان أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن إبراهيم بن العباس والفقيه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : محمد ابن الحسين ابن محمد بن الهيثم أبو عمر البسطامي الواعظ الفقيه على مذهب الشافعي ولی قضاء نيسابور وقدم بغداد وحدث بها عن أحمد بن عبد الرحمن ابن الجارود الرقى وسليمان بن أحمد الطبراني وأبي بكر القباب الأصبهاني وأحمد بن محمود بن خرزاد الأهوازى حدثني عنه الحسن بن محمد الخلال وذكر لى أنه قدم بغداد في حياة أبي حامد الاسفراینی قال وكان إماماً نظاراً وكان أبو حامد يعظمه ويجله حدثنى أبو صالح أحمد بن عبد الملك المؤذن وأبو بكر محمد ابن يحيى بن إبراهيم النيسابوريان قالا توفى أبو عمر البسطامي بنيسابور في سبع وأربعمائة . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل . قال : محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن الهيثم بن القسم بن مالك أبو عمر البسطامي القاضى الإمام توفى سنة ثمان وأربعمائة وأعقب الموفق والمؤيد .
And in Iraq, Abu Bakr ibn Malik and Abu Muhammad ibn Masa and their peers, and he heard (hadith) in Basra and Ahwaz. His appointment as judge of Nishapur arrived, and the appointment was read to us on the morning of Thursday, the third of Dhu al-Qi'dah in the year 388 AH, and he was seated in the seat of judgment in the mosque of Raja at that hour. The people of hadith showed joy and rejoicing and scattering (of coins) whose description would be lengthy. And we wrote with supplication and thanks to the Sultan, may God support him, and to his supporters. The shaykh Abu Bakr Yahya ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Salmasii related to me in Damascus, from his father, the judge Abu Tahir ibn Abi Bakr, who said: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Nasr ibn Kaka al-Muradi al-Faqih said, mentioning the master Abu Uthman Ismail ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Sabuni, who said: He mentioned the judge Abu Umar al-Bastami, saying: He was uniquely possessed of the subtleties of lordship, relying on positions of delegation. He traveled between the great Sultan and the caliphal court during the days of al-Qadir bi'llah. The people of Baghdad were captivated by his speech and beneficence, and he excelled in presenting and issuing with the soundness of his mastery. He exhibited, in that prophetic assembly and the imamite gathering, things that amazed his peers, and the guardians conceded excellence to him. They said: 'Someone like him should serve as deputy for that Sultan, supported by divine guidance and victory, and as a delegate to such a court.' Until he returned, his saddlebags filled with various kinds of honor, and his arrows (i.e., endeavors) achieving the utmost aspiration. Then he was a Shafi'i in knowledge, a Shurayhi in judgment, a Sihbani in eloquence, a sorcerer of the tongue. The sharif Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Abbas, the faqih Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur, and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham Abu Umar al-Bastami, the preacher, the faqih according to the Shafi'i madhhab, was appointed judge of Nishapur. He came to Baghdad and narrated there from Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Jarud al-Raqqi, Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Tabarani, Abu Bakr al-Qabab al-Isbahani, and Ahmad ibn Mahmud ibn Khurzad al-Ahwazi. Al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Khallal narrated to me from him, and he mentioned to me that he came to Baghdad during the lifetime of Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. He said: He was a leading scholar and a debater, and Abu Hamid used to venerate him and honor him. Abu Salih Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Mu'adhdhin and Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Ibrahim al-Naysaburiyan narrated to me, saying: Abu Umar al-Bastami died in Nishapur in 407 AH. And the shaykh Abu al-Hasan Abd al-Ghafir ibn Ismail wrote to me, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Haytham ibn al-Qasim ibn Malik Abu Umar al-Bastami, the judge, the imam, died in 408 AH, and he left behind al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry (tarjama) for Abu Umar al-Bastami, compiled by Ibn Asakir through multiple chains of transmission. It begins with an account of his appointment as judge of Nishapur in 388 AH, describing the joy of the hadith scholars. Then it presents a laudatory description from a group of scholars, praising his eloquence, judgment, and diplomatic role between the Sultan and the Caliph. Next, Ibn Asakir cites al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's biographical notice, giving his full name, his Shafi'i affiliation, his teachers, and his veneration by Abu Hamid al-Isfara'ini. Finally, two reports about his death are given: one in 407 AH and another in 408 AH, with mention of his sons al-Muwaffaq and al-Mu'ayyad. The entry highlights his scholarly and political status.

Abu Umar al-Bastami was a highly respected Shafi'i judge and scholar who served as a diplomat and was praised for his eloquence and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says he was 'Shafi'i in knowledge, Shurayhi in judgment, Sihbani in eloquence.' Which of these three—knowledge, justice, or eloquence—do you most lack in your own life, and what concrete step will you take this week to improve it?
?
The people of Baghdad were 'captivated by his speech and beneficence.' When was the last time your words captivated someone for the sake of good? Pledge to use your tongue to influence someone positively today.
?
He traveled between the Sultan and the Caliph as a trusted mediator. In your life, you often mediate between people. Are you known as a peacemaker? Commit to a specific conflict you will help resolve this week.

The Biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali: A Shafi'i-Ash'ari Judge
Ibn Asakir relates the biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly credentials of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a prominent Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge and theologian.

Core Idea
Al-Bajali was a trustworthy judge, Shafi'i jurist, and Ash'ari theologian who authored works in usul.

This lesson presents a biographical entry from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kidhb al-Muftari, detailing the life of Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Amr al-Bajali. The passage traces his teachers, judicial appointments, madhhab affiliation, and death date, highlighting his status as a faqih, usuli, and mutakallim. By examining this entry, we gain insight into the transmission of Ash'ari-Shafi'i scholarship in 5th-century Baghdad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of al-Bajali's biography.
Notice the isnad (chain of transmission) at the beginning.
2
Identify key details
Note his teachers, judicial appointments, madhhab, and his lineage tracing back to a Companion.
3
Understand his scholarly identity
The passage describes him as 'faqih usuli mutakallim' and 'Shafi'i Ash'ari'. Reflect on what these terms imply about his expertise.
4
Consider the isnad and sources
Notice the multiple chains of transmission (Ibn Asakir via al-Khatib and al-Shirazi). This shows how biographical information was preserved and verified.
5
Reflect on the significance
Why would Ibn Asakir include this biography? It affirms the Ash'ari affiliation and scholarly credibility of al-Bajali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن بن قبيس وأبو منصور بن زريق قالا قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : عبد الواحد بن محمد بن عثمان أبو القسم بن أبي عمرو البجلي ، سمع أحمد بن سلمان النجاد وجعفر الخلدى والحسن بن محمد بن موسى بن إسحق الأنصارى ومحمد ابن الحسن ابن زياد النقاش ، وهبة الله بن محمد بن حبش الفراء وجعفر بن محمد بن الحكم المؤدب ومحمد بن على بن علون المقرى كتبنا عنه وكان ثقة ، تقلد القضاء من قبل أبى على التنوخي على دقوقا وخانجان ومن قبل أبي الحسن الجزري على جازر ثم ولى قضاء عكبرا من قبل أبي الحسن بن أبي محمد بن معروف وكان ينتحل في الفقه مذهب الشافعي ويعرف أصول الفقه وسمعته أملى على نسبه فقال أنى محمد بن عثمان بن إبراهيم ابن محمد بن خالد بن إسحق بن الزبرقان بن خالد ابن عبد الملك بن جرير ابن عبد الله البجلی صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، توفى ابن أبي عمرو في اليوم الذي مات فيه ابن مهدى وهو يوم الاثنين الرابع عشر من رجب سنة عشر وأربعمائة ودفن من الغد في مقبره باب حرب أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن السمرقندى قال ثنا أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي لفظا قال : أبو القسم عبد الواحد بن عثمان بن البجلي ويعرف بابن أبي عمرو ومات سنة عشر وأربعمائة وكان فقيهاً أصولياً متكلما له مصنفات حسنة في الأصول وذكره أبو الفضل بن خبرون في الوفيات فقال الفقيه الشافعى الأشعرى .
The two shaykhs, Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur ibn Zurayq, informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib narrated to us: Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn Uthman Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Amr al-Bajali. He heard from Ahmad ibn Salman al-Najjad, Ja'far al-Khalidi, al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ishaq al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Naqqash, Hibatullah ibn Muhammad ibn Habash al-Farra', Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hakam al-Mu'addib, and Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ulwan al-Muqri. We wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. He held the position of judge under Abu Ali al-Tanukhi over Duquqa and Khanjan, and under Abu al-Hasan al-Jazari over Jazar, then he was appointed judge of Ukbara under Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ma'ruf. He professed the Shafi'i madhhab in fiqh and knew the principles of fiqh (usul al-fiqh). I heard him dictating his lineage, saying: I am Muhammad ibn Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Khalid ibn Ishaq ibn al-Zubayrqan ibn Khalid ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Jarir ibn Abd Allah al-Bajali, the Companion of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. Ibn Abi Amr died on the same day that Ibn Mahdi died, which is Monday, the fourteenth of Rajab in the year 410 AH, and he was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab Harb. The shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi narrated to us orally, saying: Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Uthman al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi Amr, died in 410 AH. He was a faqih, an usuli, a mutakallim, and he authored excellent works in usul. Abu al-Fadl ibn Khayrun mentioned him in the Obituaries, saying: The Shafi'i, the Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi Amr. It begins with an isnad from Ibn Asakir through al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, then lists his teachers, confirming his reliability as a hadith transmitter. It details his judicial appointments in various towns, his Shafi'i jurisprudence, and his knowledge of usul al-fiqh. His full lineage is given, tracing back to a Companion. The date of his death is recorded as Monday, 14 Rajab 410 AH. A second chain from al-Shirazi adds that he was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim, and authored works in usul. Finally, Ibn Khayrun's obituary identifies him as Shafi'i-Ash'ari. The entry thus highlights his scholarly credentials and his theological affiliation with Ash'arism.

Key Terms

قضاء
الشافعي
أصول الفقه
الأشعري
فقيه أصولي متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Bajali was merely a judge without theological expertise.
Correction: But the passage confirms he was a mutakallim (theologian) and authored works in usul al-fiqh.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali was a trustworthy Shafi'i-Ash'ari judge and theologian who authored works in usul al-fiqh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Bajali was both a judge (practical role) and a scholar of usul and kalam (theoretical knowledge). Do you tend to separate your religious learning from your daily work or responsibilities? What is one area of your life where you could intentionally apply a principle from usul al-fiqh or aqeedah this week, and how will you do it?
?
The passage emphasizes his lineage back to a Companion of the Prophet (ﷺ). Do you ever think about your own spiritual lineage—who you learned from, who influenced your faith? Are you taking steps to be a trustworthy link in that chain for those after you, or are you neglecting that responsibility? What will you do today to honor that trust?

Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali: A Shafi'i Judge and Ash'ari Theologian
Biography of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali with emphasis on his Ash'ari and Shafi'i identity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a biographical entry from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari establishes the Ash'ari affiliation of a Shafi'i judge, demonstrating the integration of Ash'ari theology with mainstream fiqh and qada.

Core Idea
Ash'ari scholars were not just theologians; they were judges and jurists.

This biography from Ibn 'Asakir's work presents the life of Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali, a Shafi'i qadi who was also a mutakallim. The passage demonstrates how Ash'ari identity was not a separate sect but a theological stance embraced by leading Shafi'i scholars. It also provides a chain of transmission, showing how such biographical knowledge was preserved and validated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the chain of narrators at the beginning.
The passage begins with a chain from two shaykhs to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
2
Identify key roles
Identify the roles mentioned for al-Bajali: qadi, faqih, usuli, mutakallim. Note the explicit labels 'Shafi'i' and 'Ash'ari'.
He was a judge in multiple cities and authored works on usul al-fiqh.
3
Connect to context
Reflect on the significance of a Shafi'i judge being described as Ash'ari. What does this tell about the acceptance of Ash'ari theology in mainstream Shafi'i circles?
The Ash'ari school was often associated with Shafi'i fiqh.
4
Analyze the biographical method
Notice how the biography uses multiple chains of transmission and witnesses to establish credibility. Consider why this method is important for historical theology.
The second witness, al-Shirazi, confirms the death date and adds the description 'faqih usuli mutakallim'.
5
Reflect on misconceptions
Think about the common misunderstanding that Ash'ari scholars were only theologians. This biography shows a scholar who was also a judge and jurist.
The passage counters the idea that Ash'aris were isolated from legal practice.

ومنهم أبو القسم بن أبي عمرو البجلي البغدادی رحمه الله ) أخبرنا الشيخان أبو الحسن بن قبيس وأبو منصور بن زريق قالا قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب : عبد الواحد بن محمد بن عثمان أبو القسم بن أبي عمرو البجلي ، سمع أحمد بن سلمان النجاد وجعفر الخلدى والحسن بن محمد بن موسى بن إسحق الأنصارى ومحمد ابن الحسن ابن زياد النقاش ، وهبة الله بن محمد بن حبش الفراء وجعفر بن محمد بن الحكم المؤدب ومحمد بن على بن علون المقرى كتبنا عنه وكان ثقة ، تقلد القضاء من قبل أبى على التنوخي على دقوقا وخانجان ومن قبل أبي الحسن الجزري على جازر ثم ولى قضاء عكبرا من قبل أبي الحسن بن أبي محمد بن معروف وكان ينتحل في الفقه مذهب الشافعي ويعرف أصول الفقه وسمعته أملى على نسبه فقال أنى محمد بن عثمان بن إبراهيم ابن محمد بن خالد بن إسحق بن الزبرقان بن خالد ابن عبد الملك بن جرير ابن عبد الله البجلی صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، توفى ابن أبي عمرو في اليوم الذي مات فيه ابن مهدى وهو يوم الاثنين الرابع عشر من رجب سنة عشر وأربعمائة ودفن من الغد في مقبره باب حرب أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن السمرقندى قال ثنا أبو إسحق إبراهيم بن على الشيرازي لفظا قال : أبو القسم عبد الواحد بن عثمان بن البجلي ويعرف بابن أبي عمرو ومات سنة عشر وأربعمائة وكان فقيهاً أصولياً متكلما له مصنفات حسنة في الأصول وذكره أبو الفضل بن خبرون في الوفيات فقال الفقيه الشافعى الأشعرى .
Among them is Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him. Both shaykhs Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur ibn Zuraiq reported to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib informed us: 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn 'Uthman Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali heard from Ahmad ibn Salman al-Najjad, Ja'far al-Khalidi, al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Ishaq al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Naqqash, Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Habsh al-Farra', Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hakam al-Mu'addib, and Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Alun al-Muqri'. We wrote from him, and he was trustworthy. He assumed the position of judge on behalf of Abu 'Ali al-Tanukhi over Duquqa and Khanjan, and on behalf of Abu al-Hasan al-Jazari over Jazar, then he assumed the qada' of 'Ukbara on behalf of Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi Muhammad ibn Ma'ruf. He adopted in fiqh the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and knew usul al-fiqh. I heard him dictating his lineage, saying: I am Muhammad ibn 'Uthman ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Khalid ibn Ishaq ibn al-Zubayrqan ibn Khalid ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn Jarir ibn 'Abd Allah al-Bajali, the Companion of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Ibn Abi 'Amr died on the same day that Ibn Mahdi died, which was Monday, the fourteenth of Rajab in the year four hundred and ten [AH], and was buried the next day in the cemetery of Bab Harb. Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi reported to us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Shirazi narrated to us orally, saying: Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Wahid ibn 'Uthman al-Bajali, known as Ibn Abi 'Amr, died in the year four hundred and ten [AH]. He was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim, and he authored excellent works on usul. Abu al-Fadl ibn Khabrun mentioned him in his death notices, saying: He was a Shafi'i Ash'ari faqih.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali, an influential scholar with explicit Ash'ari affiliation. It begins with a chain of narration from two shaykhs who heard from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who provides details: his teachers (including well-known figures from Baghdad), his trustworthiness, his judicial appointments in several towns, and his Shafi'i fiqh and knowledge of usul al-fiqh. His lineage is traced back to a Companion, showing noble ancestry. His death date is given relative to Ibn Mahdi. A second witness from al-Shirazi confirms his death in the same year and adds that he was a faqih, usuli, mutakallim with good works. Finally, Ibn Khabrun explicitly states that he was a Shafi'i Ash'ari. This entry documents the Ash'ari presence among Shafi'i scholars and judges.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ash'ari scholars were only theologians, not involved in fiqh or qada.
Correction: This biography shows that al-Bajali was a Shafi'i judge, faqih, and usuli in addition to being a mutakallim, demonstrating that Ash'ari theology was integrated with mainstream legal practice.

Checkpoint
What madhhab in fiqh did Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi 'Amr al-Bajali follow?
A) Hanafi
B) Maliki
C) Shafi'i
D) Hanbali

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Qasim al-Bajali exemplifies the integration of Ash'ari theology, Shafi'i fiqh, and judicial practice in 5th century Baghdad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your life will one day be summarized in a few lines. What roles would be mentioned? Would anyone describe you as a person who integrated deep theology with practical service like al-Bajali? What is missing today that you must begin building?
?
Al-Bajali's teachers are listed, his pupils perhaps unmentioned but his legacy continues. Who have you taken knowledge from, and what will pass through you to the next generation? If you are not in a chain of transmission, why not? What is stopping you from becoming a link?

A Noble Ash'ari: The Biography of al-Sharif Abu Talib
Biographical entry confirming a Sharif's Ash'arism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ash'ari theology was embraced by noble lineages like the Hashimites, as exemplified by al-Sharif Abu Talib.

Core Idea
Even a Sharif followed the Ash'ari madhhab.

This brief biography from Ibn 'Asakir records the death of a Damascene Sharif and his theological affiliation. It may seem like a simple notice, but its inclusion in this work carries weight: it shows that Ash'arism was not a marginal movement but was adopted even by those with noble Hashimi lineage. Let's examine how this single entry refutes later misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical notice
Read the Arabic and translation to get the facts: name, death, teachers, and theological madhhab.
2
Notice the chain of transmission
Ibn 'Asakir uses a chain from al-Akfani to al-Kittani to the subject. This reminds us that biography was a serious science.
3
Reflect on the significance of the statement
The final phrase 'yadhhabu ila madhhab Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' is the punchline. Why would Ibn 'Asakir include this detail? Understand the apologetic value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الشريف أبو طالب بن المهتدى الهاشمي الدمشقی رحمه الله ) أخبرنا الشيخ الأمين أبو محمد هبة الله بن أحمد الأكفاني قال حدثنا أبو محمد عبد العزيز بن أحمد الكتاني قال توفى شيخنا الشريف أبو طالب عبد الوهاب بن عبد الملك بن المهتدى بالله الفقيه يوم الاثنين العاشر من شهر رمضان سنة خمس عشرة وأربعمائة حدث عن أبي عبد بن إبراهيم بن مروان وغيره بشئ يسير وكان فقيهاً حافظاً للفقه يذهب إلى مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله
Among them is al-Sharif Abu Talib ibn al-Muhtadi al-Hashimi al-Dimashqi, may Allah have mercy on him. The trustworthy shaykh Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad al-Akfani reported to us, saying: Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Kittani narrated to us, saying: Our shaykh al-Sharif Abu Talib 'Abd al-Wahhab ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Muhtadi billah, the faqih, died on Monday, the tenth of Ramadan in the year four hundred and fifteen [AH]. He narrated from Abu 'Abd [Allah] ibn Ibrahim ibn Marwan and others a small amount. He was a faqih, a memorizer of fiqh, and he followed the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice of al-Sharif Abu Talib, a Hashemite noble (sharif) from Damascus. The chain includes al-Akfani and al-Kittani. The notice gives his death date, his limited hadith transmission from a few teachers, and his expertise as a faqih and hafiz of fiqh. Crucially, it concludes by stating that he 'yadhhabu ila madhhab Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' (he went to the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari). This explicit statement is significant for showing that Ash'ari doctrine was adopted even by descendants of the Prophet, countering claims that Ash'arism was a bid'a or contrary to the sunna.
